The Nantong Fisheries Association has applied to the provincial and county governments for the implementation of a relief plan.

Pinghu

Hengsheng Money Shop Closes Down

The Hengsheng Money Shop in front of the Chenghuang Temple in this city has been open for 35 years. Recently, due to poor business and years of losses, it was calculated that the deficit was over 80,000 yuan during this winding-up period. Shareholder Yu did not want to continue to subsidize it, so it was decided to close down and liquidate. Starting the other day (the 8th), registration of claims began, and debtors were urged to repay their debts as soon as possible.

Page 12

Municipal News Participates in London Art Exhibition

Yesterday Began Pre-Selection of Antiquities

To Be Pre-Exhibited in Beijing and Shanghai Before Transport to England

The British London Chinese Art Exhibition has already leased the Billington Building in London as its venue and is scheduled to officially open in November of this year. The exhibition will fully introduce all Chinese antiquities and art from past dynasties to the international community. Its nature is quite important, so it seeks to be comprehensive in its collection of exhibits. From ancient times to 1800, precious Chinese antiquities from all dynasties are included in the collection. The Chinese government has also agreed to transport some of the rare treasures stored in Shanghai for display. Special commissioners from the British authorities have come to China to select them together with the Chinese government. In the future, the British government will be fully responsible for the protection of these antiquities during transportation to London.

Selection of Antiquities

For the sake of selecting antiquities, the Chinese government has now designated Chuan Yiwen, section chief of the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior; Tan Keheng, staff member; Wang Rong, head of the managing section; and Zhang Jinheng of the Chinese Antiquities Preservation Committee, four people, who arrived in Shanghai the other day and contacted Ouyang Daoda, section chief of the Shanghai Office of the Palace Museum, to discuss everything. Yesterday morning, led by Section Chief Ouyang, they opened the warehouse on Zhutang Street and began the selection. A portion of the antiquities has already been selected. The selection will continue today. The antiquities that have already been selected will be sealed in another room in order to be sent to the China Bank pre-exhibition venue on Renji Road in time for arrangements. The antiquities selected by Section Chief Chuan and others from the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior, etc., in Zhutang Street are the antiquities previously stored in that warehouse by the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior and have nothing to do with the antiquities stored in Shanghai by the Palace Museum in Beijing. Section Chief Chuan and others were very careful when selecting yesterday, because this Chinese art exhibition in London is of great importance to the reputation of Chinese art. Therefore, the selected antiquities are all the most exquisite.

Beijing and Shanghai Pre-Exhibitions

After the Palace Museum's antiquities were freely transported to Shanghai, the Chinese authorities originally planned to hold a public exhibition. However, due to the large number of boxes and complicated procedures, as well as the lack of suitable locations, it was temporarily suspended and could not be realized. Now that the antiquities will be selected and transported to England for exhibition, it has been decided to take this opportunity to hold pre-exhibitions in Beijing and Shanghai before the antiquities are transported to England to publicly exhibit them so that the public can understand the exact number of antiquities. The exhibition location in Shanghai has now been found on the second floor of the China Bank on Renji Road on the Bund, because the bank has completely moved into its new location for office work. The venue will soon be arranged, and it is scheduled to open in early March. After the exhibition in Shanghai closes, it will be transported to Beijing for exhibition and then transported to England to participate in the Chinese Art Exhibition.

Request for Protection

According to the Public Works Bureau, Chinese artworks will be transported to London, England, for exhibition. Before the shipment, the Preparatory Committee plans to hold a preliminary exhibition at the former site of the China Bank on the Bund and has requested the Public Works Bureau to provide special protection. According to the opinion of the Police Department, it is not necessary to charge a fee for specially dispatching police to provide protection, but it cannot assume responsibility for the safety of the items. Furthermore, the arrangement of the exhibition venue must be handled in accordance with the conditions of the Public Works and Fire Departments. The Public Works Bureau has replied to the committee with this intention. It is heard that the exhibition is scheduled to be held in mid-March.

Commissioner Comes to China

In order to select antiquities together with the Chinese government, the British government has now specially dispatched a team of five famous Chinese art collectors as commissioners to China for selection. They have already departed from England and are expected to arrive in Shanghai in early March. The list of commissioners is recorded below: (1) Omofopoulos, British art expert and collector, president of the Oriental Ceramic Society; (2) Hobson, British art expert, currently director of the Department of Ceramics and Ethnology at the British National Museum, author of "On Chinese Ceramics"; (3) Yeats, famous British artist; (4) David, member of the Executive Committee of the Oriental Ceramic Society, member of the Chinese Committee of the Universities of London; (5) Raffael, member of the Archaeological Society, honorary assistant of the Department of Oriental Antiquities of the British Museum, member of the Executive Committee of the Oriental Ceramic Society.

Continued Verification

Regarding the verification work of the antiquities stored in Shanghai by the Palace Museum in Beijing, it was temporarily suspended a few days ago because Shu Chushi left Shanghai for business. It is learned that Mr. Shu will return to Shanghai today, so the verification work can continue today. Since the beginning of the verification of all the antiquities stored in Shanghai by the Palace Museum, more than 500 boxes have been verified so far.

Hunan Fellow Townsmen Gave Public Farewell Banquet to Minister He Yesterday

The newly appointed Turkish Minister He Yaozu is about to leave the country to take up his new post. Fellow Hunan townsmen in this city gave a public farewell banquet for him at the Atlantic Western Restaurant at 12:00 noon yesterday. Over twenty people attended, including Zhou Daoyu, Qin Zhen, Cheng Qian, Zhang Shizhao, Ye Kaixin, Chen Jie, Liu Jingyin, Zhou Di, Nie Lusheng, Hong Ziyi, Sun Yongmou, Chen Queting, Shen Zuru, Zhang Bingwen, Li Wuyun, etc.

Chen Jie Delivers a Speech

Saying, "Today, fellow townsmen and colleagues are happily giving a farewell banquet to Minister He Guiyan. Personally, I have three congratulatory points: (1) Speaking of Minister He personally, he is a famous general of the party and the country and is taking on an important diplomatic mission. As Su Laoquan said, 'A man who cannot be a general can be an envoy, and settling matters with words is enough.' Now that Minister He is taking on a diplomatic mission as a famous general, his responsibility is not just settling matters with words. This is the first. (2) Speaking of fellow Hunan townsmen, after Zeng and Guo, there have been almost no one in diplomacy for fifty years. Now Minister He is rising to fame and succeeding, and his future achievements are immeasurable. This is the second. (3) Speaking of the Chinese nation, Turkey and China were both 'sick men of the East' in the imperial era. However, with more than ten years of struggle, political reform, diplomatic victory, judicial independence, and expansion of civil rights, it has become a strong Islamic country, which can be used as a reference for our country. Moreover, Chinese Muslims are found throughout Shaanxi and Xinjiang provinces and have a close historical relationship with Turkey. This time, Minister He will surely obtain a deep relationship between the two countries, both in national relations and in national sentiment.' and so on." Then,

He's Reply

Briefly saying, "Today, I am very grateful for the grand intentions of you all. This time, the government has appointed me as an envoy to Turkey to handle diplomacy. With my meager learning, I originally did not dare to rashly take on the responsibility. However, my request to decline was not granted. Furthermore, considering the current crisis of the country, which is in a critical moment, I could not refuse the responsibility of a commoner. I can only exhaust my meager strength in order to repay the country. I would like to state a few points to you all: (1) Turkey is a newly emerging independent and free country. Examining the elements of its strength, it is due to the soundness of its nation's inherent culture and the solidity of the country's organization, which have created today's glorious position. Looking back at our country, these elements are far inferior. Under this comparison, we cannot but imitate, strive, and make progress as soon as possible. (2) The direction of a country's diplomacy should be an extension of its internal affairs. Therefore, in order to achieve diplomatic results, the focus is on the progress of domestic politics. Although I am temporarily leaving the country, I am constantly praying for the unification and solidarity of the country and the construction and prosperity of the economy. If the country itself can make real progress, it will not only promote the determination of countries around the world to recognize China's desire for independence and freedom, but also make it impossible for strong countries to infringe. Turkey was able to gain the sympathy of countries around the world and achieve the effect of recovery because of this. This is also something that our country can learn from. (3) After I leave the country, I should report my findings at any time, but I hope that you all in the country will provide instructions and assistance at any time so that we can make contributions to the party and the country from both inside and outside." and so on.

The Chinese Commercial Delegation to the Philippines is Scheduled to Depart by Ship

Wang Zhengting and Wang Xiaolai are the Leader and Deputy Leader

Scheduled to Depart on the 20th and Return to Shanghai on March 15th

At the banquet given by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on April 25th of last year, jointly with various Shanghai organizations, for the Philippine Commercial Inspection Delegation, the former chairman of the Chamber, Wang Xiaolai, proposed in his welcoming speech that a Chinese Commercial Inspection Delegation should be organized this year to go to the Philippines for inspection, to jointly seek the development of commerce between China and the Philippines, and to further strengthen the ties between the two countries. The above-mentioned opinion was submitted to the 73rd Standing Committee meeting of the Chamber and approved for the organization of the [Chinese Commercial Sightseeing Delegation to the Philippines].

Preparations are Completed and Personnel are Recommended

After days of preparations by Wang Xiaolai and others, Wang Zhengting was recommended as the leader, Wang Xiaolai as the deputy leader, Liu Zhanen as the English secretary, Pan Gongzhan as the Chinese secretary, and Chen Xiangtao, president of the China Travel Service, as a staff member. Reservations were made for cabins on the President Jackson with the American Dollar Steamship Company, and Zheng Yuanxing, manager of the Maochang Egg Factory in Shanghai, was dispatched by the Philippine office to take care of the arrangements in order to become familiar with the situation. The travel expenses were budgeted and determined by the China Travel Service, and each member was to prepare their own funds.

Meeting Convened and Passport Exemption

The delegation convened a meeting in the conference room of the Municipal Council at 4:00 PM yesterday, attended by Wang Zhengting, Wang Xiaolai, Kang Hou, Du Yuesheng (represented by Wang Xiaolai), Pan Gongzhan, Li Dachao, Yue Fucheng, Zheng Yuanxing, Qian Ya, Zheng Chengqing, Xu Xiaochu, Wang Tianshen, Chen Xiangtao, and others, more than ten people. The meeting was chaired by Wang Xiaolai, and after reporting, it was discussed and decided that the Chinese Commercial Delegation to the Philippines should be jointly guaranteed by the Dollar Steamship Company and the China Travel Service, exempting them from overseas passports in order to save procedures.

More Than 30 Members in Total

At the time of the meeting, the members who signed up, in addition to the leader Wang Zhengting, the deputy leader Wang Xiaolai, and the secretaries Pan Gongzhan and Liu Zhanen, included Pan Gongzhan's wife, Wang Xiaolai's wife, Du Yuesheng and his wife, Zhang Xiaolin and his wife, Lin Kanghou, Yu Zuoting, Xu Xiaochu and his wife, Chen Xiaodie and his wife, Cheng Yujie, Yue Fucheng, Hu Xiyuan, Xiang Hongchang, Du Jinsheng, Wang Tianshen, You Jusun, Jiang Zhuoyun, Qian Shoutie, Yu Yefeng, Shen Changgeng, Guo Shun, Zheng Yuanxing, Yu Xingben, Fang Yexian, and other male and female members, more than 30 people.

Departing This Month and Returning to Shanghai Next Month

All members are scheduled to depart on the morning of this month,

and take a small steamship from the New Customs Wharf to Balianjing in Pudong, and then board the President Jackson of the American Dollar Steamship Company. They will arrive on the shore on the 25th and conduct inspections in the Philippines. They are scheduled to return on the President Wilson of the same company on March 9th and arrive in Shanghai on March 15th. According to Chen Xiangtao, president of the China Travel Service, negotiations have been successfully completed with the Dollar Steamship Company, which will provide a 30% discount. The round-trip fare including meals is approximately 315 yuan in national currency for first-class cabins and approximately 218 yuan in national currency for second-class cabins. The journey will take a total of 23 days.

The Philippine Business Community Sends Telegrams of Welcome

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce in the Philippines the other day, informing them of the departure of the Chinese Commercial Delegation to the Philippines and inquiring about the situation there. It is learned that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has received a welcome message from the Chamber of Commerce, the original text of which is as follows: [To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, we have learned of the arrival of your delegation in the Philippines, which is very welcome. The cost of lodging and meals is from three pisos (Philippine currency worth fifty cents in U.S. dollars) to eleven pisos per day, including meals. Please telegraph the date of departure, the number of people, and the names of the members, Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce]

Promoting Publications with Philippine Propaganda

The group, to mutually plan for the development of Sino-Philippine commerce, specially assigned personnel to collect various types of national product samples from industrial and commercial organizations in this city, photograph and engrave them, and compile and print a large number of publications to take to the Philippines for extensive promotion, it is said.

Huang Fu Extends Medical Treatment

Blood Pressure of 104, Lower Than Normal

Huang Fu, Chairman of the North China Political Affairs Commission, has been recuperating at home for several days, declining social engagements. Social Construction: Issues of Marriage and Funeral Rites

丨Mayor Wu's Report at the Municipal Government's Memorial Week丨

Current Rituals are Chaotic and Lack Standards

Corrections Should Be Made to Ensure Social Conformity

Central News Agency reports: The Shanghai Municipal Government held Premier's Memorial Week yesterday morning at the Municipal Government Auditorium. Several people, including staff from the Municipal Government Secretariat and various bureaus, attended. Mayor Wu Tiecheng led the ceremony and reported on [Issues of Marriage and Funeral Rites in Social Construction]. His original words are as follows:

Fellow comrades, at the last joint memorial week, I gave a comprehensive report on the municipal government's policy guidelines for this year and explained that this year is the "Social Construction Year" for this city. I hope that all colleagues will, within this year of the Republic of China's 24th year, work diligently on the construction of social undertakings, based on the principles of social construction. However, there are many social undertakings that need construction. Our time, financial resources, and manpower do not permit us to complete them all in one, two, three, or four years. Moreover, social undertakings are never completely finished in a single day because society is progressing every day. We should naturally also be innovative and strive tirelessly, keeping pace with the times. Therefore, we can only select a few of the most urgent social undertakings within the scope permitted by our time, financial resources, and manpower to undertake this year. However, in addition to the social undertakings we stipulated last time, there is another matter related to social morality that needs to arouse the attention and research of all colleagues in our municipal government, and also the attention and research of all citizens of Shanghai, which is matters of marriage, funerals, and celebrations.

This is something that we all consider a very important event in one's life. However, the marriage, funeral, and celebration rituals currently popular in society are mostly equivalent to child's play, simply without any rituals to speak of. In the past, our country had fixed rituals for coming-of-age ceremonies, weddings, funerals, and sacrifices, and everyone respected them equally. These old rituals were certainly very cumbersome and did not conform to the spirit of the modern era. However, after abolishing the old rituals, we have not yet established new rituals. What is currently popular in society is neither Eastern nor Western, neither ancient nor modern. Each person has their own way, today is different from tomorrow, and tomorrow is different from the day after, making society almost a society without rules. Everyone does as they please. How can we unite such a chaotic and disorderly society?

We know that the first requirement for a healthy social life is to be able to unite and have discipline. To make society united and disciplined, we must give this society a common custom, so that all the individuals living in the whole society have a common standard to abide by. Only then can this society be united and disciplined, and the foundation of this society can be stable. However, Chinese society today is neither Eastern nor Western, neither modern nor ancient. There are no definite rituals, making us all at a loss and causing contradictions everywhere. We see that the funeral processions on the streets of Shanghai now are, in many ways, just like joyous events. Moreover, the ceremonial guards are originally intended to express solemnity, but they are filled by people who are extremely undignified. Their spirit and posture are not neat, and the clothing they wear is especially bizarre. The music played by the military band often plays happy music for funerals and funeral music for happy events, fully demonstrating that our society has no rules and no rituals. Once, a cosmetics company held a ceremony for the completion of a new factory and invited me to attend. At that time, the music team suddenly started playing national music when they shouldn't have. The audience all stood up, but the musicians were sitting and didn't stand up, and they didn't play in unison. Two of them only started playing halfway through the song. We can't list all the similar things. In short, there is disorder everywhere. There are also no definite rules for weddings. Even the so-called civilized weddings have several problems. First, the bride and groom exchange rings, but they don't exchange them personally; instead, the male and female attendants exchange them on their behalf. Second, they don't personally stamp the marriage certificate; instead, the male and female attendants represent them. Third, the speeches at the wedding are mostly treated as child's play, and many obscene words are even used, without any solemnity. Therefore, whenever someone asks me to officiate at a wedding, I must make three rules: First, the bride and groom must exchange rings personally; second, they must stamp the certificate personally; and third, no one is allowed to tell jokes or use obscene words during the wedding, lest they undermine the solemnity of the wedding.

Weddings and funerals are two extremely important events in society. These two extremely important events in society show that Chinese society has no rules, no rituals, and no organization; it is just a mess. In this situation, how can we unite society, make society excited, and make society move? Establishing rituals and making music are certainly the powers of the central government, but the situation of such a lack of rituals in society, even to the point of absurdity, cannot be allowed to continue indefinitely. Therefore, we should also pay attention and make corrections. I have already ordered the Social Bureau to ban the bizarre costumes of commercial military bands and order them to play happy music for happy events and funeral music for funerals, with definite rules. At the same time, I have also ordered the Public Security Bureau to ban funeral processions. However, such passive prohibition is not enough to be effective. Therefore, a definite standard must be set so that everyone in society has something to follow, in order to prevent the current situation of lacking standards, disorder, and chaos from appearing in the future Shanghai society. This is also something that all colleagues in the municipal government should pay attention to and work hard on when working on social construction this year of the Republic of China's 24th year. Secondly, everyone must remember that the anniversary of the New Life Movement will soon arrive. We should work harder to realize the ideals of the New Life Movement by improving the general customs of society.

The Minsheng Company's "Minkang" Ship Sinks

At Duntou, 30 Miles from Hankou

All Crew Members Rescued; Losses Exceed 100,000

Guowen News Agency reports: The "Minkang" ship of Sichuan's Minsheng Industrial Company sank at Duntou, 30 miles from Hankou, on the afternoon of the 8th due to shallow water and hitting a reef. Yesterday, the reporter inquired at the Henan Road branch in this port, and the information obtained is as follows:

Minsheng's Operations

The headquarters of Minsheng Industrial Company is located in Chongqing, with a branch in this port. The general manager is Mr. Lu Zuofu. The company has 27 river steamers and shallow-water vessels, exclusively sailing along the Yangtze River and the Jialing River and Qu River banks. The "Minkang" originally sailed on the Shanghai-Chongqing line. Recently, due to shallow water in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, it only sailed to Yichang. The ship was built in England and has a larger hull than other ships, with a gross tonnage of 618 tons and a net tonnage of only 262 tons. It has been sailing between Shanghai and Chongqing for five years.

Details of the Reef Collision

This time, the "Minkang" loaded cargo in Shanghai last month and sailed upstream. After arriving in Yichang, due to the military situation of bandit suppression in northern Sichuan, it was dispatched to Hankou empty on the 5th of this month. Unexpectedly, at 12 noon on the 8th, when the ship arrived at Duntou, 30 miles from Hankou, it mistakenly hit a reef due to shallow water and rapid currents. The hull suffered severe damage and sank immediately. At that time, the crew prepared to rescue the ship, but it was too late. The captain urgently sent a distress signal. Fortunately, a nearby small ship heard the alarm and rushed to the rescue. Moreover, the ship did not carry passengers or cargo besides the crew, so there was no danger to life. The ship has now completely sunk, and all crew members have been rescued and are temporarily staying at the Hankou branch, awaiting further arrangements.

A Glimpse of the Losses

Although the ship has sunk after hitting a reef, it was an empty ship and not loaded with goods. When it slowly sank, all the crew members' belongings were also transferred to a small ship. Therefore, the only losses are the ship's hull and furniture, amounting to more than 100,000 yuan. However, the ship's hull was insured with a foreign company for marine insurance, so no significant losses are expected. Whether to salvage the ship or not will be decided after the Chongqing headquarters sends personnel to survey the situation. Due to a delay in airmail, the Shanghai branch has not yet received a written report on the details of the accident.

Another source reports that the ship was insured with a North American insurance company for 70,000 yuan. The current captain is Yuan Changfa, it is said.

Shanghai-Kunming Airline to Open Soon; Ford Aircraft Shipped to Shanghai

Vessel Loaded in America is En Route

Expected to Arrive in Shanghai in Late February

Shen Shi News Agency reports: China National Aviation Corporation, to open the Shanghai-Kunming airline, which passes through the Yangtze River line to Kunming, Yunnan, conducted a test flight earlier with satisfactory results. Considering that the route, though not long, passes through continuous mountains and steep peaks, requiring a sturdy, large aircraft, it ordered a large Ford aircraft from the aircraft manufacturing department of the Ford Motor Company in America last October for this purpose. According to the Shen Shi News Agency's sources at China National Aviation Corporation, the aircraft was completed in America half a month ago and was shipped by the Maersk Line (Gertrude Maersk) a week ago. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai in late February. This is a large, three-engine aircraft with 1,450 horsepower, a speed of 135 miles per hour, ten passenger seats, and two pilot seats, accommodating ten passengers in total. It is equipped with both land-to-air and air-to-land wireless radios, costing a total of 40,000 US dollars, or about 150,000 Chinese yuan. The company plans to install the aircraft as soon as it arrives in Shanghai to conduct a second test flight to Kunming in mid-March. If everything goes well, the direct Shanghai-Kunming airline should be open by the end of March or early April.

Officially Sending and Receiving Commercial Telegrams

Shen Shi News Agency reports: The Shanghai Radio Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications previously proposed opening the radio station of Special Envoy Huang Musong in Lhasa, Tibet, for commercial use. After several test transmissions with good results, the circuit, which passes from Lhasa through Ganzi and Chengdu to Shanghai, is now officially open. Wireless Communication Has Not Been Interrupted

Jianmu Industry Declining; Lumber Merchants Appeal for Relief

Petition to Revoke Bankruptcies and Cancel Harsh Taxes: Details of the Situation

Fujian is one of China's leading timber-producing provinces, but has declined in recent years due to banditry and political upheavals. Recently, the delegation of petitioners from the Min River Upper Reaches Fir Timber Industry Association issued a notice detailing the bankruptcy of Jianben and the petition to cancel harsh taxes, as follows:

Our country is rich in timber resources, which not only supply domestic needs but also sell abroad in considerable quantities. Among the timber-producing areas, apart from the three northeastern provinces, Fujian is the most prominent. Hence, it is named Jianmu after the region. Among the Jianmu production areas, the four prefectures of Yanping, Jianning, Shaowu, and Tingzhou in northwestern Fujian are the most abundant. The livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people in these prefectures depend heavily on this industry. Before the 11th year of the Republic, the annual output was 40,000 to 50,000 chains, worth over 10 million yuan. Recently, it has sharply declined, falling to no more than 10,000 chains this year, worth 3 to 4 million yuan. The reason for the decline lies in the disturbances of the Red disaster, which destroyed the rural areas, and the excessive taxation, which increased costs. The sales prices did not match, and businesses repeatedly failed. Timber merchants stopped operating one after another, mountain prices were affected and lowered, timber farmers intermittently planted trees, timber workers lost their jobs and took risks, and social unrest occurred. All of these are based on this. However, Jianmu has suffered such devastation that it is on the verge of bankruptcy. Foreign timber has seized the opportunity to invade the entire country at low prices, and the economy has overflowed outward. The future of national and people's livelihoods is extremely worrying. To save this predicament, we must eliminate the Red bandits, revive the rural areas, abolish harsh taxes, and protect domestic timber. (1) The Red disaster: The production of timber in northwestern Fujian is abundant, and the livelihoods of the people depend on it. However, since the 17th year of the Republic, the Communist bandits occupied western Fujian, and in the 19th year, they spread to northern Fujian. Wherever the bandits went, they burned, plundered, raped, and killed, making people unable to live. Fields were desolate, and rural areas were ruined. The timber industry was therefore abandoned. Fortunately, the central government's suppression was effective, and the Fujian bandits were pacified within a year. Unfortunately, the vitality was damaged, and recovery was not easy. Survivors after the disaster are heartbroken to speak of it. (2) Exploitation by harsh taxes: The procedures for purchasing fir timber, including cutting, digging, dragging, releasing, loading, and transporting, all have fixed times, requiring at least five or six months. In addition, the capital is very large, and the loading and transportation are heavy. Transporting along the river to Fuzhou is as long as eight or nine hundred miles, and recently it has exceeded two hundred miles. In addition, the Min River has rapid currents, and there are fixed stations for berthing. It is impossible to be fast. Corrupt local bullies, local ruffians, and bandits along the way are well aware of the above-mentioned relationships and know the inside story, arousing thoughts of coveting and extortion, resorting to any means to demand fees. As a result, the number of donation and tax items has exceeded 30. Although the government has repeatedly issued prohibitions, it is beyond reach. There is nothing that can be done. In addition, legitimate tax items are often inflated by corrupt officials. Timber merchants suffer from this exploitation and cannot bear it. (A) A brief history of the temporary housing assistance fee at Shuikou: Judging from the name, it is known that this levy is neither a tax nor a donation, but a temporary fee, which is meaningless. The period when this fee was established was in the 21st year of the Republic, when the central government clearly ordered the abolition of the escort donation collected by miscellaneous troops on the Min River. The 19th Route Army did not dare to violate the central government's order. On the one hand, it wanted to recover what it had already collected. At that time, it immediately gathered stream merchants and discussed the matter. It was claimed that the escort fee was cancelled by the order of the Ministry, but since Liu and Lu's troops had no way to raise funds, the temporary defense assistance fee was changed to be established at Shuikou, collecting 45 yuan for each chain of timber rafts with 13 or more bottoms, and 40 yuan for each chain with 15 or fewer bottoms. It was limited to six months and would not be extended. Adding to the burden of merchants and people, no matter what, they temporarily endured it with difficulty. At that time, there were thousands of chains of timber rafts accumulated at Shuikou. Timber merchants, due to capital relations and under the coercion of warlords, had little power to resist. They had to endure the levy, thinking that it was only temporary. Unexpectedly, it has been more than two years, and the warlord rebellion has been defeated. Liu and Lu's military pay has been issued by the central government. The Red disaster has gradually subsided, and the Fujian situation has been stabilized. However, the harsh donations created by the rebels to harm merchants and people still exist and have become even more serious. In the past, the reporting procedures and escort patrol boats were handled by members of our association who set up offices on behalf of customers. Recently, the office has also taken on patrol boats, soliciting protection fees, taking the opportunity to supplement reports, and doing whatever they want. Timber merchants suffer twice as much as before. Although they have repeatedly appealed to the office, it has been ineffective. (B) A brief history of the business tax in Zhuzhi: After the party center clearly ordered the abolition of lijin, the Fujian provincial authorities created a consumption tax due to a sharp decline in revenue, stipulating that 5% would be levied per 100, with producers and consumers sharing half each. The bureau was originally set up in Hongjiang Zhongzhou to collect taxes. During the tenure of Mr. He Gonggan as director of the Finance Department, it was moved to Zhuzhi. When the central government promulgated the business tax regulations, it was levied on the category of bamboo and wood sales, set at 2/1000. Merchants and people should pay the legitimate tax set by the central government. Unexpectedly, the tax bureau violated the order of the Ministry and forcibly collected 5%, paying taxes per chain, about 25 yuan. Even randomly increasing the levy to 6% or 7% when reporting, practicing the consumption tax in the name of the business tax. The principle of business tax is to levy taxes in the location where the business is located, but Zhuzhi is located in the hinterland of the Min River, not the business location of timber rafts. Setting up a bureau to collect taxes halfway is a clear violation of the regulations. Now that the rebel He has been defeated, the remnants of his evil deeds should have been corrected long ago under the rule of the pure and upright party, to comply with the orders of the Ministry and to alleviate the people's suffering. (C) Other harsh taxes: Public welfare, education, military service, culture, charity, and protection donation in Nanping County; schools, hospitals, and education donations in Gutian County; land protection, raft watching, and garrison wine fees at various stations along the way; debt allocation for the Minbei Highway; etc., are no more than 30 types, collecting from a few jiao to several yuan arbitrarily, leaving people with no choice. (3) Cost and sale price: Jianmu is assembled into chains, with many types, depending on the length and size of the wood. The names are also different, such as 9-bottom, 11-bottom, 13-bottom, 15-bottom, 18-bottom, and 21-bottom. (A) Cost: The mountain price per chain is about 156 yuan, the cost of cutting, dragging, and releasing is about 80 yuan, miscellaneous expenses and interest are about 30 yuan, the cost of loading and nailing is about 20 yuan, the cost of transportation and wages is about 90 yuan, and legitimate taxes and harsh taxes are about 80 to 90 yuan. The total cost per chain is about 400 yuan. (B) Sale price: Taking the 13-bottom timber as an estimate, each section sells for 3 yuan, the 15-bottom sells for 2 yuan, and the 18-bottom sells for 1 yuan. Then, each chain of timber rafts is only worth over 300 yuan. Comparing the cost and sale price, the loss is significant. The bankruptcy of Jianmu is undeniable. (4) The petition process and results: Timber merchants, due to excessive burdens and losses of capital, have stopped operating one after another. Jianmu is therefore bankrupt. The future of hundreds of thousands of people in more than 20 counties in northwestern Fujian is worrying. Therefore, timber merchants have repeatedly come to the association to voice their concerns. Examining the actual situation, the suffering is unbearable. Our association could not bear to sit idly by and has repeatedly submitted telegrams to the central government's competent authorities, seeking relief and requesting that harsh taxes be abolished and illegal tax rates be corrected. The instructions were received, "Order the Fujian provincial government to investigate and handle." It was then submitted to the Fujian provincial authorities, requesting that they be revoked and corrected. A reply was received, "Since this defense expenditure is a major local revenue, and the military is in urgent need of funds during the bandit suppression period, it is difficult to revoke it temporarily. As for the business tax on bamboo and wood, it is collected according to the old rate and has been in place for a long time, making it even more difficult to approve changes immediately." In this way, the timber merchants could not bear it. In December of the past year, the joint meeting of the three associations decided to nominate Chen Xinyuan and Xuan Yongsheng as representatives to go to Beijing to petition the central government's various ministries and commissions, requesting that they quickly order the revocation in order to alleviate the people's suffering and save the timber industry. The central government's various ministries and commissions were sympathetic to the merchants' difficulties. The Ministry of Finance telegraphed on the 18th of December, letter No. 1164, "The telegrams from December 23rd are noted. We have already telegraphed the Fujian provincial government to strictly order the swift revocation of the Shuikou defense fee and the correction of the business tax rate in Zhuzhi." After receiving the order, we immediately nominated comrades Huang and Liu to represent us in visiting the chairman of the Fujian provincial government and the director of the Finance Department. We submitted two reports, requesting that they be implemented separately in accordance with the orders of the Ministry. However, there was no reply, only a verbal answer that the finances were difficult and it was inconvenient to revoke them. Not getting the point, we sent Chen Xinyuan and others to Beijing for a second petition. We received another telegram from the Ministry of Finance on January 21st, letter No. 1801, "The report from January 22nd and the association's wireless telegram are noted. We have already telegraphed the Fujian provincial government again to follow the previous case and strictly order them to comply. You should be informed immediately." The Executive Yuan issued an instruction on January 31st, No. 46, "The report is noted. This case has been submitted to the Yuan for handling by the Central Government. It has been instructed to be submitted to the Fujian provincial government for handling together. You should be informed immediately." The instructions from the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang and the People's Movement Guidance Committee have been forwarded to the Executive Yuan for review. The Military Affairs Commission has also issued an instruction, "Send it to the Ministry of Finance for review." The representatives have repeatedly stated everything to the central competent authorities. They have also received instructions from various ministries and commissions, ordering the Fujian provincial government to strictly order the revocation of the Shuikou defense fee and the correction of the heavy business tax in Zhuzhi. We should wait quietly for the Fujian provincial authorities to comply with the orders of the Ministry and implement them separately. (5) Appeal to the public opinion circles for assistance: The petition to revoke the defense fee and correct the business tax on bamboo and wood has been clearly ordered by the central competent authorities to comply. This proves the central government's determination to abolish harsh taxes. However, the suffering of the timber merchants is difficult for the people of the country to hear everywhere. However, public opinion is the mouthpiece of the people. To make the whole country understand the decline of Jianmu, the invasion of foreign timber, and the reasons for the unemployment of the people of Fujian, we still need the assistance of the news media to arouse the attention of the people of the country and jointly save the crisis. Abolishing harsh taxes is to relieve Jianmu. Relieving Jianmu is to resist foreign timber, so that we can recover our rights and benefit the people. We have always admired you as leaders of the press and the eyes and ears of the people. Please provide assistance with correct public opinion, so that hundreds of thousands of timber people in Fujian can celebrate their rebirth. We will be infinitely grateful.

Mayor Wu Also Scheduled to Host on the 26th

Polish Envoy in China Informs the Chamber of Commerce Explaining the Reason for Heavy Taxes on Chinese Goods

Due to Failure to Submit Proof of Origin

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from Wu Zemin, a merchant residing in Poland, stating that he had been living in Poland for many years and that the hand-woven grass baskets from our country were very popular with the Polish people. He entrusted Shanghai Xindali to purchase and transport them to Poland for sale. Unexpectedly, after arriving at the port, the customs officials of that country excessively raised tariffs. The cost was less than one Chinese dollar, but they demanded three times that amount. The tax levied on grass baskets transported from Czechoslovakia to Poland was less than 80% of the value. The difference was enormous. He requested the Chamber of Commerce to step forward and strongly protest. The Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the previous day, requesting them to negotiate based on reason and to strive to ensure that Chinese goods exported to Poland would not be hindered or stalled. This was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday, the Polish Legation in China sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce explaining the reasons for the heavy taxes on Chinese goods. The original text is recorded below:

To the esteemed members of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce,

In recent days, various Chinese newspapers in this city have published a letter from Mr. Wu, a Chinese merchant, addressed to your esteemed Chamber, stating that a number of grass baskets were transported to our country for sale, but were heavily taxed by our customs officials, while similar goods transported to Poland from other countries were taxed very lightly. Our Legation is aware that this complaint does not conform to the facts, and that the reasons for the heavy taxation have not been stated. We dare to inform you of a few things so that your esteemed Chamber can understand the details of this matter.

According to the Treaty of Commerce signed between our two countries on September 18, 1929, all Polish goods transported to China and Chinese goods transported to Poland for sale shall be granted most-favored-nation treatment. The volume of Chinese goods exported to our country each year is quite large. Our customs officials have always assessed them according to regulations, and we have never heard any complaints from Chinese merchants.

During the past ten months, the value of certificates of origin for commercial goods issued by our Legation and used by Chinese merchants going to Poland amounted to 1,117,0517 customs gold units. The types and prices of these goods are listed below:

㈠ Soybeans and sesame: 891.609

㈡ Peanuts: 328.13

㈢ Tea: 35.05

㈣ Cinnamon and other spices: 13.174

㈤ Pig bristles: 7.29

㈥ Albumin: 4.487

㈦ Egg yolk: 9.537

㈧ Antimony: 13.743

㈨ Bean cake: 7572

㈩ Tung oil: 3.646

㈩㈠ Mutton tallow and other fats: 3.086

㈩㈡ Other oils: 20.195

㈩㈢ Pig intestines: 28.540

Reviewing the above statistics, it is clear that there is such a large volume of trade between our two countries, and no disputes have ever occurred. Why would our customs officials apply differential treatment only to goods worth just over six gold pounds? Perhaps this is Mr. Wu's first time doing business in Poland, and therefore he has not followed the regulations. As a rule, when Chinese merchants transport goods to Poland, they must submit a certificate of origin to our Legation for verification and stamping. Our customs officials will then assess and release the goods based on this certificate. Mr. Wu only submitted a bill of lading to our Legation, without the certificate of origin issued by the Ministry of Industry of your country. After the goods arrived in our country, he did not present the stamped bill of lading for verification, claiming that the bill of lading had been lost en route. Therefore, our customs officials identified the type of goods according to the customs tax list. Also, because the raw materials of the grass baskets transported by Mr. Wu were not recognized by anyone in our country, and he could not present the certificate issued by the Commodity Inspection Bureau of your country, the customs officers considered these grass baskets to be made of a special type of grass, and levied the highest level of tax.

Furthermore, the gross weight of the grass baskets transported by Mr. Wu to our country was 243 kilograms, but the packaging accounted for 110 kilograms. Therefore, a large portion of the customs duties paid by Mr. Wu was consumed by the packaging.

Our Legation also has a similar experience. Last year, a certain exporter from our country transported some salted pork to this country for sale. Your country's customs officials considered it cured meat and levied a tax that was fifteen times higher than the tax on salted meat. The exporter paid a total of 250 Chinese dollars in taxes, and then sold the salted pork in Shanghai, actually earning 160 dollars, including the customs duties. Our Legation believed that the reason why the Polish merchant paid heavy taxes was that he could not present the certificate of the Commodity Inspection Bureau of our country certifying that it was salted meat, so there was no way to negotiate for him. Although the Polish merchant suffered a significant loss, he did not write to the press to complain about the injustice.

If your esteemed Chamber examines the above, you should be able to understand everything about the origin of this matter.

Hong Mian, Investigator of Anhui Disaster, Reports on the Disaster Situation in Zhide County, Anhui

Drafting Plans for Purchasing Grain to Save the Dying, Providing Agricultural Loans, and Assisting Livelihoods

The Shanghai Office of the Central Relief Committee recently received a telegram from Hong Mian, who investigated the disaster in Anhui, outlining plans for purchasing grain to save the dying, providing agricultural loans, and assisting livelihoods. The report on the situation in Zhide County was extremely concise and detailed, making it unbearable to read. It is hereby disclosed, hoping that benevolent people will work together to provide relief.

To Xu Jinglao of the Shanghai Renji Hall Relief Committee and all the great philanthropists in Shanghai,

I have heard that the righteousness of disaster relief is like putting out a fire, and the method of providing relief is even more important than saving the dying. Therefore, to save the disaster-stricken people who are on the verge of death, without precise planning and swift action, it is impossible to turn death into life and reverse the great catastrophe. I, Mian, was ordered to come to Anhui to investigate the disaster situation. According to statistics, the number of disaster-stricken counties has reached as many as forty-nine. Among them, Zhide is the most severely affected. Because Zhide borders Pengze, Fuliang, Poyang, and other counties in northern Jiangxi, it has little land and many mountains, and has always been known as a poor area. Since the winter of the 22nd year of the Republic, the communists have spread throughout the county, looting food and slaughtering even the village dogs. In the summer of the 23rd year of the Republic, they approached the county seat, and their momentum became even more rampant. After repeated suppression, they have not been eradicated. The people have fallen into displacement and suffered the most severely. Coupled with the rampant drought, the land is barren. Old reserves are exhausted, and new harvests are nonexistent. The young and strong have already taken risks, and the old and weak have filled the ditches. Some have been burned and looted by bandits and suffered from drought, resulting in the destruction of their houses. They have freed themselves to return, while others have suffered severely from drought and are on the verge of starvation, resulting in a continuous stream of people on the road, seeking food in other towns. All of them are barely clinging to life, on the verge of death. According to statistics, there are about 56,000 people in total. These large numbers of disaster-stricken people have already become starving corpses, exposed to the wind and dew. Observing their tragic situation, some are eating grass roots, tree bark, or Guanyin flour, resulting in poisoning and bloating to death. Some families are starving and cannot borrow money, resulting in mutual cannibalism. Some are selling their sons and daughters, with each child selling for only a few dollars, resulting in the separation of flesh and blood, and the sound of crying is miserable. And the elderly and sick, suffering from hunger and cold, are collapsing on the road, unable to be buried. The sights are too horrible to bear.

Such a combination of banditry and drought, with the disaster not yet over, is truly a rare disaster that has not been seen in recent decades. I believe that the future is long and the great difficulty is behind us. Those who are hungry are barely clinging to life, and those who are about to die will eventually not be willing to sit and die. It will be seen that when they can no longer bear it, they will rise up and join the bandits, which will inevitably lead to the tragedy of disaster-stricken people becoming bandits and bandits becoming disaster-stricken people. The year is already coming to an end, and collapse is to be feared. Next year's spring plowing will have no seeds, and the famine can be predicted. The current situation is so serious, and the hidden dangers are growing so deeply. The disaster machine will be triggered at any moment, like a prairie fire. Looking ahead, it is chilling and frightening. I am not trying to be alarmist. Therefore, under these circumstances, saving the dying is the most urgent priority, followed by assisting livelihoods. Saving the dying is nothing more than urgent relief, while assisting livelihoods is mainly agricultural loans. Urgent relief is a temporary solution, temporarily saving people from death, while agricultural loans are a fundamental solution, sufficient to support the livelihoods of the coming year. The so-called treatment of both the symptoms and the root cause is actually the way to eliminate bandits. Only when the bandits are eliminated can the people be at peace, and only when the people are at peace can the country be governed.

Although we have received relief from various parties, it is like a drop in the bucket, and it is difficult to expect relief. I deeply believe that financial resources are exhausted, and it is difficult to raise money. Without precise planning, how can we save such a widespread and extraordinary disaster? I have been thinking hard day and night, not even having time to eat or sleep. I plan to first raise funds in the short term to purchase grain and provide urgent relief to save the dying, and then, depending on the amount of additional funds raised, provide agricultural loans to assist livelihoods. The main point of urgent relief is to use funds wisely and for a long period of time, saving more people, so that it can be effective. I plan to follow this principle, starting from now until the wheat season in early summer next year, for a long-term relief period of three months, so that those who are barely clinging to life can continue to exist and not abandon spring plowing. The method is to distribute one catty of red grain per person per day, regardless of age. This amounts to 28,000 catties of grain per day, 840,000 catties of grain per month, and a total of 2.5 million catties of grain in three months. According to the market price of 6 yuan per shi of Bengbu rice, with each shi being 200 catties, this amounts to 140 shi of Bengbu rice per day, costing 840 yuan. Each month, this amounts to 4,200 shi of grain, costing 25,200 yuan. In three months, this amounts to 12,600 shi of grain, totaling 75,600 yuan. In this way, for a period of three months, more than 56,000 people can be saved, and the funds used are very small. On average, each person only receives a few yuan, which can save their lives. There is truly a wonderful effect of using minimal funds to achieve great results. There is no better plan than this. Once this plan is implemented, if donations are abundant, reaching more than 75,000 yuan, the remaining funds can be used to provide agricultural loans, so that they can purchase seeds, plowing cattle, and farm tools, and plant in time to support their livelihoods for a year, so as to avoid disaster on top of disaster, leading to a major change, to the point of being irreparable. As for the procedures for providing relief and the methods for agricultural loans, I will explain them in detail later. The matter is urgent and fleeting, and the opportunity to do good is nowhere to be found. I have always admired the great philanthropists for their willingness to provide relief to the masses, regardless of regional boundaries. Therefore, I dare to express my sincerity and appeal on behalf of the 56,000 disaster-stricken people, hoping that the great philanthropists will be moved by the current situation and worry about the future, and will definitely not give way to others, but will generously donate and widely solicit donations, gathering together to complete this concrete plan. Then, the field of blessings will be widely sown, and the merits will be boundless. Heaven's will can be reversed, and human disasters can be avoided. There will truly be an inconceivable feeling of summoning auspiciousness and harmony. I respectfully kowtow nine times on behalf of the 56,000 disaster-stricken people, and earnestly hope that you will show great compassion and help to make this happen. I cannot express my urgent hope enough.

Hong Mian kowtows.

No Other Reason

Appeal of the Murderer in the Tang Jiapeng Case

Supreme Court Judgment

In Addition to Murder, an Additional Charge of Possession of Firearms

The Court Transferred a Document to Wuchang to Investigate the Facts of Wang's Crime

After Tang Jiapeng, also known as Ah Yu, the former manager of the Great World Amusement Park, was assassinated in front of the Great World at around 1:00 AM on June 18 of the 22nd year of the Republic, Jin Jiujin, the detective superintendent of the French Concession Police, and detectives from a special agency arrested the murderers, Zhang Xiaosizi (i.e. Tinggui) from Funing and Zhao Guangfu from Yangzhou, one after another, and retrieved a pistol used by Zhao to kill Tang, and sent them to the Second Special Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution for premeditated murder. After the trial concluded, Zhang Xiaosizi was sentenced to twenty years in prison and Zhao Guangfu was sentenced to life imprisonment, and each was deprived of public rights for life. The two criminals were dissatisfied with the judgment and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. As a result, the appeal was rejected and the original judgment was upheld. Zhang then no longer appealed, the sentence was finalized, and he was sent to prison. However, Zhao was still unwilling to accept and appealed again to the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court reviewed the entire file and ruled that in addition to the original judgment on the murder, an additional charge of possession of firearms was added. The main text of the judgment stated that the original judgment regarding Zhao Guangfu's crime and sentence was revoked. Zhao Guangfu was sentenced to life imprisonment for jointly premeditated murder and deprived of public rights. He was sentenced to one year in prison for intending to use the handgun for criminal purposes, and the sentence was to be served with life imprisonment. The handgun was confiscated. This judgment will be sent to the Second Branch of the High Court in the coming days for execution in accordance with the law.

In addition, based on Zhao's confession, the French Concession Police recently arrested Wang Xinggao, a major criminal from Funing who instigated the killing of Tang, and sent him to the Second Special Court for interrogation. Wang hired lawyers Yan Shen and Xingxia to defend him, denying that he had instigated the killing of Tang Jiapeng. At the time of the incident, he was the warden of the First Prison in Wuchang. The court has now transferred a document to the Wuchang Court for investigation. The trial will be held as soon as the Wuchang reply is received, and the date should not be far off.

Woman Injured Suspiciously

Refuses to Explain the Reason for the Injury

Some Say it was a Former Lover Seeking Revenge

Chen Heshang, a local man, is 34 years old and lives at 19 Dunheli, Latou Road, French Concession. His wife, Wang Lingli, from Ningbo, is 28 years old. Chen and Wang were originally living together. Chen Heshang was originally a chauffeur at the Huayang Automobile Company on Beidi Road, but is now unemployed. At 9:00 PM last night, Wang was holding a teapot and went to the Xingfa Teahouse at 298 Nongkou to brew tea. Wang put the teapot on the stove and went outside. The people in the teahouse saw that she was an acquaintance, so they did not ask any questions. Unexpectedly, Wang returned not long after, and they saw that her body was covered in blood stains and she was walking unsteadily. They were greatly surprised and asked her what had happened. She stammered and said that she had been stabbed in the gambling house. At this time, Chen Heshang also received the news and ran out of the house in a hurry. He saw that his wife's face was pale and she had lost all color. He questioned her about what had happened. She claimed that she had been stabbed in the gambling house. Chen reported to the police, who sent a car to take her to the Guangci Hospital for treatment. After the doctor's examination, it was found that she had four knife wounds, one on each breast and two on the upper back. The injuries were very serious. According to rumors, it is suspected that Wang's former lover came to seek revenge. The police are currently investigating.

President Kong's Broadcast at the Nanjing Central Broadcasting Station

Celebration Meeting and Shanghai Infant Health Competition Held

The Children's Year will commence on April 4th of this year. The specific measures for holding the Children's Year have been carefully discussed and drafted by the Ministries of Education and Interior, and will soon be jointly submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation nationwide. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the Chinese National Child Welfare Association held a meeting of officers at noon yesterday (the 11th), and has assigned several specialists to earnestly prepare for the Association's own activities on the opening day of the Children's Year. In addition to participating in various activities of the Shanghai Children's Year Preparatory Committee together with various Shanghai institutions (Municipal Government, Education Bureau, Health Bureau, Public Security Bureau, Municipal Party Headquarters, Children's Welfare Association, etc.), the Association will also: (1) gather children from the Association's affiliated Tzu Yu Education Institute, Civilian Education Institute, and Tzu Yu Nursery on April 4th to hold a large-scale celebration meeting (to be prepared by Ms. Yao Shuwen and Ms. Wang Zhubao); (2) the Association's affiliated Tzu Yu Clinic will hold the Shanghai Infant Health Competition (to be prepared by Dr. Huang Huiguang, Dr. Liu Yide, Ms. Xia Shi, etc.); (3) on the eve of the opening day of the Children's Year, President Kong Xiangxi will deliver a speech at the Nanjing Central Broadcasting Station [on the significance of holding the Children's Year]; (4) publish "A Message from the Chinese National Child Welfare Association to the National Compatriots on the Opening Day of the Children's Year" (to be drafted by Chen Zhengfan); (5) edit a "Children's Year Handbook" and suggest to the Central Children's Year Preparatory Committee that it be published jointly by the Chinese National Child Welfare Association and the Central Children's Year Preparatory Committee (to be edited by Chen Zhengfan); (6) be responsible for assisting Shanghai newspapers in editing a "Special Issue for the Opening of Children's Year and Children's Day Celebrations." In addition to the existing inscriptions and congratulatory messages received from various important figures in the National Government and prominent figures in society, it will continue to solicit essays, inscriptions, drawings, etc., from various important figures, celebrities, and scholars to achieve perfection and completeness (to be edited by Chen Zhengfan); (7) other unfinished matters will be planned by Chen Tiesheng, Wang Guanyi, Chen Zhengfan, etc. Furthermore, during the meeting of officers held by the Association on the 28th of last month, it was agreed in principle to make the following four suggestions to the National Government: (1) on the opening day of the Children's Year, the Chairman of the National Government should issue a declaration of the Children's Year to express the government's determination to protect children; (2) on the opening day of the Children's Year, the chief administrative officers of the capital and various parts of the country should hold ceremonies to inspect child welfare institutions, in order to show the importance attached to child welfare undertakings; (3) during the Children's Year, the government should specially allocate large sums of money (such as the Boxer Indemnity) to provide relief to homeless children throughout the country; (4) the Central Political Council should establish a Children's Welfare Committee (or add a Child Welfare Department to the Ministry of Interior) to guide, assist, and control child welfare undertakings throughout the country. However, because these four matters are of great importance and involve complex issues, it is still necessary to conduct research from a practical perspective. Therefore, the entire body elected Chen Tiesheng to consult with President Kong Xiangxi for a final decision. However, due to President Kong's recent minor illness, he has not yet been able to report the matter. It is expected that after President Kong's research and approval in the coming days, it will enter a stage of practical implementation.

Changes in the Design of the New Building

Reduction in the Number of Floors Due to Market Depression

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the original site of the Bank of China on Renji Road on the Bund is old and has been affected by the adjacent new construction projects, causing internal tilting. Therefore, the bank authorities planned to rebuild the tallest building in the Far East, a 28-story new building, and move entirely into the office at the intersection of Hankou Road and Sichuan Road during the Spring Festival holiday. A previous report stated that the bank, in view of the market downturn, was considering temporarily suspending construction. According to information obtained by reporters from reliable sources, the bank's new building was originally planned to be a 28-story building. As for the construction project, it will not be suspended because the current office, which was moved to last year, is temporary and does not meet the needs.

Lianyi Association of Vegetable Market Stallholders in the Second Special District

Reply to the Letter from the French Concession Police Department

Requesting Legal Protection of Members' Interests

Non-arbitrary Illegal Suppression or Deprivation

Since the establishment of the Second Special District Vegetable Market Stallholders' Lianyi Association, its members have reported to the association that they have been repeatedly oppressed by contractors, who have illegally profited from them, resulting in insufficient income. There have been hundreds of cases of complaints. The association has been doing its best to legally protect the interests of its members. On the 28th of last month, it sent a letter to Mr. Chuan, the Director-General of the French Municipal Council, requesting the French authorities to crack down on contractors who illegally profit from them. However, no reply has been received. Recently, the French Concession Police Department suddenly sent a letter stating that the association was not allowed to be established, which was astonishing. The executive committee was immediately convened to hold an emergency meeting. They unanimously declared that a reply should be made to the letter. The letter is as follows: To the Director-General: On January 3rd and 30th of this year, we received your letters No. Ai and No. 1614, which stated: [After investigation, the establishment of the Second Special District Vegetable Market Stallholders' Lianyi Association in the French Concession is not permitted. The association's officers are prohibited from exerting pressure and extorting donations from stallholders in the French Concession.] After investigation, the purpose of our association's organization is to exchange knowledge between China and France. It was approved by the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department of the Chinese Nationalist Party and reported to your office for the record. We are writing to raise three points for your detailed explanation: (1) The area of our association is within the scope of the Third Special District. Because the members have been repeatedly oppressed and defrauded of money by contractors, and in view of the organization of various groups such as the Citizens' Union in the French Concession, our association was legally established with the approval of the Party Department in order to seek protection. Now your letter states [the establishment is not permitted in the French Concession]. May we ask what legal basis is there for not permitting it? It seems that Chinese legal groups are allowed to establish themselves in the French Concession, while our association is an exception. This is doubt one. (2) [The association's officers are exerting pressure and extorting donations from stallholders in the French Concession.] Since its establishment, our association has not collected any donations. How can the association's officers be exerting pressure and extorting donations from stallholders who are not members in the French Concession? There is no evidence for this. It is all based on speculation. We think governments of all countries would not do this. This is doubt two. (3) The purpose of our association is to assist the French Municipal Council in facilitating the management of various vegetable market stalls and to protect the interests of the stallholders who are members, to crack down on illegal contractors, and to prevent oppression and illegal profits. Therefore, on the 28th of last month, we sent a letter to Mr. Chuan, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, requesting the crackdown on oppression and illegal profits by contractors. However, no reply has been received. All of our association's members are taxpayers in the French Concession. They are oppressed, and our association has certified that they have not received the obligation of taxpaying protection. Why should our association be ordered to be suppressed by your office? Upon checking the laws and regulations of the Republic of China, there is no such explicit provision. This is doubt three. We hope for an immediate clarification in order to dispel doubts and maintain public opinion. We are looking forward to it.

Public Concession

Traffic Accident Incidents

13,557 Times

Public Concession Traffic Report for Last Year

According to the report of the Police Commissioner of the Public Concession in 1934, the number of all types of vehicles increased this year, and vehicles parked on the road often remained for a long time, causing various congestion situations. However, in general, the traffic situation was satisfactory. The motorcycle team patrolled and directed at any time, which was very effective. The situation on the one-way roads was also good.

Racecourse Road

Racecourse Road is a shortcut for traffic in the central and western districts. It was used more this year, benefiting the diversion of traffic on Jing'an Temple Road and Edward Road during busy hours. However, it has not yet been fully utilized.

Prosecutions for Violations

The number of violations this year was 48,941 (53,034 last year), of which 8,668 were prosecuted, including 595 foreigners and 8,073 Chinese. 369 vehicle owners were issued driver's licenses, and 1,604 rickshaw pullers were issued licenses. In total, there are currently 17,854 licensed rickshaw pullers in the concession.

Public Transportation

The tram company currently has 107 locomotives and 107 trailers, as well as 99 trackless trams. The total number of passengers for the year was 119,687,484. There are still 164 buses, of which 8 have been converted into double-deckers. The total number of passengers was 36,936,227.

Commercial Vehicles

The number of freight vehicles this year reached 1,821. 7 vehicles were declared invalid, and licenses were withheld for 203 vehicles due to defects. 1,528 cases of overloading were investigated.

There are 39 car rental companies, a decrease of 8. The number of rental cars is decreasing. The vehicles are generally in good condition. Licenses were withheld 17 times due to poor condition of parts and damage to the car body.

Human-Powered Vehicles

Public rickshaws are still inspected every two months, and random inspections are carried out on the road at any time. Licenses were withheld for 2,200 vehicles due to violations. 23,485 rickshaw pullers were prosecuted for violations. The Rickshaw Affairs Committee has been in charge of issuing licenses since June. The average number of chartered rickshaws this year was 12,751. Strict measures were taken to crack down on chartered rickshaws soliciting passengers privately. In addition, 32,916 bicycle licenses were issued this year.

Handcarts and Horse-Drawn Carriages

The average number of handcarts was 15,227 (13,242 last year), and the average number of small carts was 7,739 (8,841 last year). The regulations for these licenses have been revised this year. The number of horse-drawn carriage companies has now decreased to 8, with only 88 carriages.

Accident Statistics

In 1934, there were 13,557 traffic accident incidents, with 4,462 people injured and 120 people killed. In 13,021 accident incidents, there were 4,112 injured, and the injuries were very minor. Among those killed, 15 were under the age of 7, 22 were between the ages of 7 and 16, 74 were between the ages of 16 and 60, and 9 were over the age of 60. Bicycle accidents were involved in 2,919 incidents. Storytellers who preached about road safety knowledge still went to teahouses and factories to tell stories at any time.

Number of Cars

The number of licensed cars in 1934 was 6,389 private cars, 1,055 public cars, 1,821 freight cars, 179 buses, 705 motorcycles, and 72 temporary licenses were issued. In 1930, there were 4,445 private cars, 1,017 public cars, 1,333 freight cars, 140 buses, 733 motorcycles, and 55 temporary licenses.

Mr. and Mrs. Tao Jia Yao's Silver Wedding Anniversary

66th Birthday and Silver Wedding Ceremony Held at the Same Time

Tao Jiayao (Xingru), currently residing on Avenue Joffre, is 66 years old. He has served as the Governor of Jiangxi Province, Supervisor of the Jiujiang Commercial Port, and Salt Transport Commissioner of Changlu. In recent years, he has retired from officialdom and lives in seclusion in Suzhou and Shanghai, not asking about national affairs. The 6th was Mr. Tao's birthday, and he hosted a banquet at the Suzhou Garden Hotel and held a silver wedding ceremony with his wife, Ms. Hua Yufang. Mr. Li Liejun, a member of the Central Committee, was specially invited to officiate the wedding. Mr. Tao has a wide circle of friends, and there were many guests from all sides. In addition to Li Liejun and his wife Hua Shiqi, well-known figures included Mrs. Yang Yongtai, Li Yinquan, Zhang Yunbo, Zhao Shuyong, former legislator Ms. Tao Xuan, and former Fifth Army Commander Zhang Zhizhong, who all personally went to Suzhou to offer their congratulations. Li Liejun and Hua Shiqi specially composed poems to congratulate them.

The Zhabei Gruel Kitchen Continues to Open This Morning

Limited to the Old, Young, and Disabled

More Than 6,000 People on the First Day

The Liuying Road gruel kitchen, sponsored by the Zhabei Charity Group, was suspended twice on the 26th of last month due to the large number of disaster victims seeking food and the inability to maintain order. In order to avoid crowding, it was stipulated that young and strong people would not be given gruel, and it was only limited to the old, young, and disabled. It reopened for the second time yesterday morning. Because yesterday was the first day, there were more than 6,000 disaster victims. It is reported that after this restriction, the feeding period may be prolonged, which is truly good news for the elderly, weak, and disabled disaster victims.

Pihan Institute's Finances Are Critically Deficient

Zhang Zixin, Director of the Pihan Institute in Southern Shanghai, reported to Wang Yiting and Huang Han'zhi, the chairmen of the Charity Groups Joint Association, yesterday, stating that the institute has been operating since December 1st of last year, and the number of people it shelters has been increasing day by day. There are now more than 2,900 people in the two institutes. Although efforts have been made to economize on expenses, the item of rice still requires about 25 stones at present. Including other expenses, the total is more than 18,000 yuan. Moreover, the spring cold is still severe, and it is difficult for the poor to leave the institute to seek a living on their own. If the end is delayed, such as extending it by one month, it will require 9,000 yuan. The current balance is only one million yuan, which is insufficient for the purpose, and the difference is very large. The income and expenditure semi-monthly report has been prepared and submitted for your review, and we earnestly request prompt relief to benefit the poor and do great deeds. It is reported that the two chairmen, Wang Yiting and Huang Hanzhi, have been raising funds from all sides in recent days. It is now reported that the Red Cross Society has donated another 50 bags of rice, and Ding Zhiren Hall has donated two loads of white rice, but it is still far from sufficient.

Victims Under Car Wheels

One Death... One Injury

Near the intersection of Xinza Road and Datong Road at 5:15 PM yesterday, a freight truck, license number 9636, was speeding east. A pedestrian, Zhu Leduan (26 years old, from Nanjing), was walking towards it. He was unable to avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, severely injuring his head. He immediately lost consciousness. Police Constable No. 2410 of the Xinza Road Patrol Division found him and transported him to Renji Hospital for treatment, but to no avail. He died at approximately 7:05 PM.

Near the intersection of Xinza Road and Chengdu Road at approximately 5:25 PM yesterday, a public bus No. 10 driving there knocked a man dressed in blue cloth clothes and pants, who appeared to be a worker, to the ground, injuring his head severely. Police Constable No. 1564 spotted it and rushed the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Mr. and Mrs. Feng Anrong Suffocate from Coal Gas Poisoning

Mr. Feng Anrong, a Ningbo native, lives upstairs at 569 Chengdu Road in the Public Concession. At approximately 8:00 PM last night, because the weather was very cold, he burned a coal stove in the bedroom for heating. However, the room was steamed for a long time, and the coal gas filled the room. Mr. Feng and his wife, Ms. Lu, were poisoned by coal gas and lost consciousness. Their neighbors discovered this and urgently called the police and an ambulance, which transported them to Renji Hospital for treatment.
