Grains Tianjin Guild Extracting This Month's Flour

After the opening of the flour market yesterday morning, the prices for each month were generally stable and rising. There were no official reports on foreign wheat, but according to private sources, prices rebounded by 3, 4, or 5 jiao. When the prices opened, the market sentiment for this month was initially stable. Soon after, due to the Tianjin guild extracting [flour], people’s confidence gradually improved. Distant months [prices] rose due to continuous spring snow. Based on past experience, [people] worried that it might affect the wheat harvest. Therefore, buying sentiment was strong, and out-of-town merchants also made some purchases, causing the market to gradually rise. Regarding the factories, it was heard that only Fufeng sold some futures, while the rest did not sell. Given the current situation, if sales to the north continue, there is still a possibility of a favorable trend for this month. As a result, this month rebounded by 3 fen, March rose by 2.5 fen, April and May rose by 3.5 fen, June rose by 2 fen, and July rose by 1.5 fen.

Wheat Market Improved by Spring Snow

Yesterday's wheat market, after opening in the morning, showed a favorable trend for all months. Due to the absence of reports on foreign wheat, people lacked a basis for their sentiment. However, the spring drought was relatively severe, and continuous spring snow, based on customary speculation, might have some slight impact on the future of the wheat market. Therefore, after the opening price, the market sentiment immediately turned positive, and trading in all months became active. Bids increased by 3 fen. Approaching the afternoon opening, the near-term market remained stable, continuing to rise by 1 fen. The distant months saw a slight weakness due to weaker buying sentiment and some sales of foreign wheat futures. As a result, this month rose by 4 fen, March rose by 3 fen, and April rose by 2 fen. Spot wheat [market was flat] because factories’ appetite was unchanged, and there were no transactions.

Rice Market Continues to Rise by a Few Jiao After Rain

(Shanghai South) Due to the initial opening of the market after the Lunar New Year, the arrival of ships seemed to be less, with only two ships arriving. The sales market in this street started to move, and the scene continued to show an upward trend. The price of Jiangsu and Tongzhou glutinous rice increased by 1 jiao, and the price of Nanhang early rice increased by several fen, approaching 1 jiao. Although the demand for late rice from Qingjiao and other districts seemed to be less than before, with only 300 to 400 packages purchased by Qingdao merchants, the final result was that people were optimistic due to the limited arrivals, and the price rose by 1 jiao. Consequently, various types of rice such as Du Yangjian and Yin Yuan also followed suit.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, more than the remaining ships from various routes arrived at the river. Due to the rain on the first day of the New Year opening, there were few sales. Yesterday, the total sales of goods from river factories in the market were about 7,000 dan. The market's appetite for various goods was flat, and local merchants' sentiment looked weak. The price of Jiashan early rice was down a few fen. The price of medium and lower-grade northern glutinous rice and thin rice also lacked vitality. The price of customer-specified top-grade rice remained stable. Other varieties were not abundant in the market, and prices remained unchanged.

Customer Xian Rice Gradually Rises by a Few Jiao

Saigon Arrivals Plentiful, Price Down 5 Fen

Yesterday's foreign rice market conditions, this office appetite, foreign rice market bottom quite low, and arrivals are constant. Since the beginning of this month, there have been six or seven ship arrivals. There is more rice in the market, and only the first day of the market opening saw smooth sales. Yesterday, only 2,500 bags of Saigon rice were opened, and the price was lowered by 5 fen. However, glutinous rice, with fewer arrivals, was able to hold steady. Only customer Xian rice, with fewer arrivals and high production prices, made transportation unprofitable. People were originally optimistic, and yesterday some Nanjing merchants tried to purchase, and local merchants also responded. Therefore, all Xian rice uniformly rose by 7-8 fen to over 1 jiao. A total of more than 3,000 bags were opened throughout the day, all purchased by local and Nanjing merchants.

Free Talk

Two Different Kinds of Romanticism

— Xin Ren

The importance of discussing the issue of romanticism, now that the slogan of realism is being given serious attention, need not be elaborated upon here. Some people may think that theoretical discussions alone are just empty talk and do not benefit reality. I do not want to completely deny this. Those articles that ignore specific realistic conditions, indiscriminately pile up the names of many foreign works, and use confused logic to parrot others, probably do more than just no good in practice. On the contrary, specific and practical introductions and studies are not only beneficial but also very necessary.

Regarding the question of what kind of romanticism we need now, there has already been a considerable amount of introduction in literary circles. Even in the November 17th issue of this journal last year, Mr. Qi's article "Realistic and Romantic" gave a brief overview. However, this issue is quite complex. Literary historians have always found it extremely difficult to review romanticism, or even displayed confusion as a result. Even today, as literary theory enters a new stage of development, there is still no correct and comprehensive understanding of this issue, although the main principles have been confirmed to some extent.

As an attempt, I am raising this issue again here. First, I want to use the results of reliable literary history to discern that there are clearly two essentially different tendencies in past romantic literature. Because in this way, when we talk about the question of "what is our romanticism," we may be able to obtain a more powerful basis.

The social cause of the rise of romanticism was the social change that occurred. In the process of social change, it mainly divided into two different tendencies: one social group walked on a dark path leading directly to the tomb of history, and the other social group marched on a "path of life" leading directly to the stage of history. In essence, these are two completely opposite tendencies; however, these two tendencies both go through the same phenomenon. To give an example, this "dark path" and "path of life," although their trends are opposite, they must both go through a dark tunnel during the period of social change. At this time, whether it is people walking on the "dark path" or people walking on the "path of life," they are surrounded by darkness; therefore, a kind of "fantasy" arises. Furthermore, because of the subjective differences in society, this "fantasy" is also divided into two opposing types: one type, although feeling the darkness around them, is because they themselves are part of this darkness, so although their "fantasy" takes on various forms, in essence, it is a eulogy to darkness; the other type also feels the darkness, but they pass through the reality of darkness, ardently yearning for the light, and fiercely hating and resisting the darkness. On these two different foundations, two different romanticisms are produced: degenerative and progressive.

Looking at the historical facts of the past makes the above words even more convincing. From the end of the 18th century to the beginning of the 19th century, the socio-economy of Western Europe underwent rapid changes. The establishment and development of the capitalist mode of production led to the gradual decline of the feudal system. At this time, classicism, as the artistic form of the feudal system, was negated and criticized by romanticism. For example, the general rational tendency of classicism, the unities, etc., were all abandoned by the emerging romanticism; but these are all the symbols of romanticism that are opposed to classicism, not the essential characteristics of romanticism. If we further seek the essential characteristics from the romanticism of various countries, then two different romanticisms will appear before us. In England, the romanticism of Scott, Byron, and Wordsworth is degenerative; the romanticism of Coleridge, Southey, Godwin, and Shelley is progressive. Similarly, in the romantic literature of France and Germany, we can also find the two types of degenerative and progressive. Those belonging to the former include Chateaubriand and Vigny in France, Fouque and Arnim in Germany, etc.; those belonging to the latter include Victor Hugo and Heinrich Heine in France, and A.H. Hoffmann and Heinrich Heine in Germany. Degenerative romanticism sympathizes with the decline of the aristocratic class, and their "fantasy" is nothing more than a funeral song for the aristocratic class; progressive romanticism, however, sings the birth song of capitalism with terrible heat. Some writers, such as Sant and Heine, are both possessors of these two romanticisms. I can only briefly summarize it here because I cannot conduct literary history research in this short article.

All new schools in history, because their subjective requirements are consistent with the development of the objective reality of history, their art is realistic. However, as described above, when a new school rises, it inevitably has the expression of "fantasy" romanticism. Does this seem like a very conflicting view on the surface? However, in fact, this view will not conflict. As mentioned earlier, progressive romanticism starts from reality. These romantic "fantasies" are just like the romantic will of a high-spirited young man who rebels against reality. Because he already has a rebellious heart towards reality, he is fundamentally different from those who dare not face reality and escape reality. At this point, we can draw a conclusion: All emerging literature in history is necessarily "realistic and romantic."

It is also for this reason that it is easy to cause misunderstandings if we traditionally say that romantic literature is "dealing with reality with a thoroughly subjective idealistic attitude" without adding considerable limits, i.e., that the romanticism referred to is a degenerative one. Because for progressive romanticism, such as Shelley, Heine, etc., in a philosophical sense, we might as well say that it is realistic.

An Ant on a Hot Pot

— Lin Qiu

In the sleepless night, in the deathly silence, I used the mirror of memory to reflect on myself over the past five or six years. What appeared in the mirror at this time was an ant on a hot pot.

Driven from the countryside to the city by an invisible and vicious whip, and then from the city back to the countryside: hitting walls, stumbling, pain, shouting, struggling; the body became thinner day by day, and the soul became thinner day by day, but still circling like this, endlessly, without exception, just like an ant on a hot pot.

Yes. The present society is a hot pot, and I am the ant on this hot pot.

One sultry summer night, I escaped from the firehouse-like attic room with a body full of sweat, lying on the cool cement floor of the balcony, silently exhaling under the double oppression of life and anger, looking at the brilliant stars. A thunderbolt-like fire alarm made me painfully sacrifice all my property within three minutes – two shelves of messy old books.

Carrying a tattered small suitcase, stepping on the cool road in the deep silence of the night, after a long period of consideration, I knocked on the door of a foreign companion's room. A small attic room with a monthly rent of five yuan, without electricity, without a washbasin, without a stove, and without a cool breeze, old newspapers were pasted on the torn walls, and three shirtless Korean youths were lying on the newspapers. After they asked a few indifferent questions, they fell asleep snoring again. I hummed a heavy sigh and found my sleeping spot at the base of the wall.

Then, as usual, I was driven from the city to the countryside by an invisible and vicious whip, to a rural elementary school. For half a year, in order to adapt to the harsh environment, I had to paint a hypocritical mask on my true face. Hypocritical to colleagues, hypocritical to students, and even more hypocritical to friends outside. Wearing a hypocritical mask, I lived a life as heavy as Mount Tai and as empty as a vacuum under the exploitative machine of extremely meaningless and extremely busy work.

I remember one Saturday night, the pain and boredom made me bravely drink more than four times my usual amount of yellow wine and fell dead drunk under the table. In the completely unconscious state of drunkenness, I vomited out the truth that had been accumulated in my chest for months like a volcanic eruption: I severely criticized the inferior behavior of each colleague. When I woke up the next day, I realized that I had caused a great disaster, but it was too late to remedy it. As a result, the cruel fate almost fell on me again.

With a trembling heart, I barely got through one semester. I could not and did not want to be here next semester. Like an ant on a hot pot, I was about to crawl from the countryside to the city again. The unbearable pain that the city had given me had been deeply buried in another kind of pain I had suffered in the past half year. At this moment, I vaguely felt that an unprecedented happy life was waiting for me in the hazy city, just like my feeling about the countryside when I left the city.

A Poor Woman Spins Yarn by the River

— TK

Sorrow Comes to Bother People

— Zang Kejia

"A thousand homes with laughter, slow to cease, anxieties creep in, known beyond things.

Standing alone on the city bridge, no one knows, Watching the star for a morning seems like moon time."

After eating the New Year dumplings prepared by myself, the firecrackers everywhere had already sounded like fried beans. While listening to Shen Ding and a friend from afar were playing chess, under a lamp, I remembered these lines of Huang Zhongze's poem.

In the feudal era, encountering a peaceful and prosperous age with no surprises, spending New Year's Eve in the countryside, that feeling was extremely mysterious. And our contemporaries insisted on leaving their reunited families. At this moment, when laughter slowly ceased in every home, they ran alone to the desolate bridgehead to look at a star. This action seemed strange, but it was not strange at all. Most of the poets in China in the past were good at seeking sorrow and finding hatred. "For writing new words, forcing to say sorrow" was the reason for "loving to go upstairs," so what was so strange about standing alone on the city bridge watching the stars?

In this New Year's Eve at the end of the world, guarding a wall of light, even a heart as hard as iron cannot avoid "anxieties creeping in, known beyond things." This night is really a bit different. You don't want to think about anything, but demons insist on making you think about them.

In this China where it is difficult to live, the end of the year is really a gateway to hell. In the city, I only feel that my wallet is tight, and I see red notices sealing the doors of some shops, and there are also those who cannot report a business closure and commit suicide by self-immolation. The economic rope is tightly fastened around everyone's neck, and so many lives are strangled to death. The countryside is originally like a thin ghost. At the first mention of the "end of the year," it immediately withers and transforms into a skeleton. Everyone carries heavy debts on their backs, and cannot even afford a cotton-padded coat on their bodies. In front of every house, you will see people arguing and fighting for money. Vicious dogs hug the sticks of debt collectors. Good people will also turn into "thieves with ulterior motives," hiding a kitchen knife in the mountain gully waiting for the God of Wealth. A bolt of cloth or a string of wood can turn you into a "person falling on the road." As the end of the year approaches, people's courage seems to suddenly increase, and tragic news is discussed and replaced by everyone.

The day before yesterday, a student living in the countryside wrote the following letter: "Now my village is bankrupt beyond recognition. All day long, I can't hear anything else, only hearing this family selling the house and that family pawning the land. Because of years of drought and insect plagues, there is no harvest at all. People lack food and clothing. In our local area, the official and private taxes that should be levied on each acre of land every year are no less than one yuan or more. If you think that food and clothing are not sufficient, where can this money come from? No one wants to pawn land. Some sell their daughters, and some run away from debt and dare not go home. There is a term. I don't know if the teacher knows it, which is "reporting the drum." This means that they cannot afford to repay the debt, and they sell all their possessions completely. Finally, they invite the creditors to a table of guests, and it is considered cleared. This "reporting the drum" happens often in my village. It is even more severe in the few days leading up to the New Year. Furthermore, the poor hang themselves because they cannot get through the New Year, and some borrow money at an interest rate of five or six cents. My family's finances are bankrupt. My dad won't let me continue next semester. I cried for three days, but there was nothing I could do! Teacher, think about what kind of world this is!"

Tonight, I thought of this poor student, I thought of the bankrupt villages and cities, and I thought of all the heartbreaking things in the world. I didn't run to the city bridge to watch the stars. Sitting under this light, sorrow came to bother my heart in the sound of firecrackers!

Old New Year's Eve

A Trip to Luokou (Part Two)

— Liu Ming

㈡ A Glimpse of Luokou

Turning over a snow-covered embankment, the slender black shadows of the iron bridge and the gray-yellow posture of the city walls appeared eye-catchingly in the snow. This was the town of Luokou we were heading for. Just now, we were still walking on a relatively smooth motor road. Now, the road leading to Luokou has become a bumpy, snow-covered, dilapidated road. After entering the city, the road became even worse. The car often got stuck in the snow and mud, making it difficult to move forward or backward. If we wanted to get out of the car, there was no place to stand. This place really felt like old China. Only the coachmen could get out of the car and help each other, slowly pushing and pulling the cars in front to overcome the difficult situation, and then move the cars behind. In this way, the car pullers were more hard-pressed, and the passengers also felt embarrassed. Originally, we wanted to go to a more lively place, but we completely gave up the idea and chose a quiet place, heading straight to the Yellow River.

The north city wall of Luokou Town is the embankment of the Yellow River. Walking on the street, we saw the upper ends of many sails exposed above the embankment. The river water was as yellow as its name suggests. It has not yet frozen. Countless ice floes, as big as houses, floated on the water, slowly flowing downstream, which was very beautiful. It was as if the thawing Volga River in the spring, which I had seen in movies before, actually appeared before my eyes. It is said that at this time last year, the river had already been frozen with very thick ice, and donkey carts and horse carts could freely pass over it.

If there were not two or three wooden cargo ships slowly sailing between the ice floes, and small boats full of passengers slowly crossing to the other side, the river would be very desolate. Because the river water was not clean, the ice floes appeared dirty, and when the sunlight shone on them, they did not reflect any brilliant light. Perhaps it was because we were standing on the south bank, facing the sun in the north.

There is a Luokou Railway Station on the river embankment. The rails are divided into two tracks, both lying in the snow. One track curves to join the Jinpu Railway, and the other stretches straight, passing under the Yellow River Iron Bridge, forming a cross shape with the Jinpu Railway. Next to the station, there were many rural teenagers, dressed up in various male and female roles, with wooden feet more than a foot high tied to their feet, performing the walking postures of old operas. Beside them, there were musical instruments such as gongs and drums playing along, just like performing a play. However, there were fewer people watching than performing, probably because they were taking advantage of this lonely snowy day to perform plays to entertain themselves.

㈢ The Yellow River Iron Bridge

Seeing the iron bridge with its steel figure lying powerfully on the Yellow River, I felt that the dirty Yellow River became even more weak and pitiful, as if it was chained with thick chains. At the same time, I vaguely felt that the fate of old China was somewhat similar to this.

The Yellow River Iron Bridge was built by German engineers. The head of the bridge is covered with German words. It is 1,250 meters long.

On the bridge, the middle is the Jinpu Railway track, and the sides are sidewalks. Just as we were about to go up and take a walk, two soldiers guarding in front of the stone house, basking in the sun and reading books, said:

"Sir, don't walk on it. You can only look at the bridgehead."

It is said that pedestrians were allowed to walk on it before, but now even tourists are forbidden to stand on it. I don't know for what reason, but the attitude and tone of the guards were very kind, unlike the soldiers of the past who, when they had guns, showed a very arrogant and disrespectful attitude towards the common people. While we were looking at the bridgehead, the soldiers who were reading were still immersed in their books. At the same time, several bald-headed guards emerged from the stone wall house and concentrated on practicing gymnastics on the scaffolding built by the roadside. Their sincere appearance was really admirable. I don't know why, but at this time I felt a great interest in these bridge-guarding soldiers, and I constantly shifted my gaze from watching the river view to them. When we were about to leave, as we walked past the two guards who were focused on reading, I took a closer look and found that they were reading "The Story of Yue Fei."

High Altitude (1)

— Written by Henri Barbusse, Translated by Di Zhou

At the fifth hour, we replenished our supplies in the interior of North Africa. We landed in the chaotic civilization of Europe, adorned with trams, streets, and cities. We walked on the road, and above, the sound of the waves of stench emitted from the nose of the plane could be heard.

··· One morning, we flew behind a large white chessboard embedded in the green coast of Africa. Our plane flew diagonally past the Strait of Gibraltar. It drew a tangent line in Spain and flew away. Our flight in the European sky was a period of testing speed in the uppermost layer of the atmosphere. Europe was under us, engulfed in a whirlwind. A slow flight at a speed of 300 kilometers per hour. The continent, the objects appearing on the island factory site, and the field of vision from 50 kilometers above. (One hour, 2,000 francs of volatile oil and kerosene).

Nights of distress and nightmares, erected between things on the ground.

Occasionally, in that infinitely long lament, came an unexpected wireless phone call. I went to visit Uncle Louis, who lived in Kyoto and had a pleasant face. Surrounded by relatives and friends, Uncle, sitting in an armchair, was still so solemn. A face full of gentle love, wearing a beautiful linen robe and velvet in the clothing court, like a romantic poet, was covered in the pale color of death.

Supplement to the Shen Bao Local Edition

Conversations

On Group Weddings and Others

— Qiong Sheng

I remember that last December, the Japan Family Science Research Society published a comparison table of marriage expenses in various countries around the world. It said that for a family with an annual income of 2,000 yuan, the proportion of marriage expenses to annual income was: England 1, France 1, America 2, Italy 4, Spain 7, Soviet Union 8, Japan 20-25, China 25-30. For those with an annual income of 10,000 yuan, the proportions were: England 0.8, France 1, America 4.2, Italy 4, Spain 5, Soviet Union 8, Japan 10-20, China 30.

But we are behind in everything, poor in everything, and helpless in everything. Only in the extravagance of marriage expenses do we almost rank first. This may be because we are a country of etiquette, so we regard the marriage of women and men as a "lifelong event." Usually, we are stingy and narrow-minded, but when it comes to marriage, we are very generous, even pulling, borrowing, and selling are not hesitated. Why bother? There is only one reason: to save face. To look good.

In this way, it is indeed difficult to make marriage a "lifelong event." Just think, to marry a wife, from hiring a matchmaker to paying dowry, asking for a name, all the way to welcoming the bride, everything must be done through the eye of Confucius. If all items are implemented in accordance with the old etiquette, how many of the 200 million men can afford it and dare to ask for it? Even marrying off a daughter, making dowries, and rushing to prepare dowries are also a costly burden. Therefore, some people say that wanting a woman is equivalent to buying a beautiful car. The price is very expensive, and the subsequent consumption expenses are also appalling. I think this is the truth of someone who has experienced it firsthand.

Social figures have seen this biased phenomenon and specially proposed a frugal marriage movement, and promoted and implemented it. This pioneering move that sees through the evils of the times is indeed of great benefit to society. Group wedding is one of them. It is said that Beijing City decided last year to solicit 50 pairs of new couples, pay a marriage fee of ten yuan, and plan to hold the wedding ceremony in the Huiren Hall in Zhongnanhai on New Year's Day this year. Although I don't know how the following article is, the fact that Shanghai will hold the first group wedding ceremony on April 3 has already happened. I think this is a great convenience for those who regard marriage as buying a car.

Arriving Home

— Yue Shan

Arriving home, I feel that my hometown is still lovely, but my feelings for my hometown are not the same as when I left home. Firstly, my hometown is very unfamiliar to me. Secondly, even at home, things are very different from before.

On the first day I arrived home, among the children who came to visit me, I recognized very few. A feeling of sadness immediately rushed to my heart: Where are my childhood companions? I couldn't help but shout! At the same time, I also felt that soon after, this group of crying companions would probably feel the sadness of losing their flock like us.

My childhood companions, like me, were whipped by life to unknown distant places. They probably don't have any lingering feelings for their hometown, do they? What does the hometown give them? It is distress, it is hunger; the hometown cannot give them comfort, life makes them have to leave their hometown and struggle in another environment! Passing through that banana garden, that black gate, is the home of one of my childhood companions. How is that home now? His father died of illness in Nanyang, thousands of miles away, and his mother became a widow for half her life, and closed her eyes under the circumstances of green teeth and white eyes. He, alone, continued to follow in his father's footsteps and wandered in Nanyang: Is there still a home in his eyes? Ah! His home! The roof is leaking! The sun, the moon, the wind, and the rain can all be swept in from that large broken place. This is his home. Can his hometown give him comfort in his heart?

Thinking of this, I was silent. How did my hometown change so quickly? In front of the ancestral hall, is there still the south wind of the past stealing? The scholars wearing long gowns and melon-skin hats, knocking on their pipes and talking about the harvest on the high steps? A society is declining, I think, and the ancestral hall is a symbol of it.

"Who is in charge of the ancestral hall's account? Why is the house so broken?" I asked my brother.

"Who is in charge? The ancestral hall has no account long ago! The grass is overgrown in the yard, who is in charge?" The ancestral hall is like this. I recalled the grand sacrifices in spring and autumn, the solemn and graceful scenes, still in my mind! But today, how many years have passed? Counting, it has only been six or seven years since I left home, right? How did it change so quickly?

"It's embarrassing! You don't know!" My brother almost sighed. He may still be nostalgic for the scenery of another society. I feel a little pity for him. He was originally a person whose spine was bent by life! His nostalgia for the declining society does not seem strange to me. I hope this society will soon come to its end, and I will welcome the arrival of another new, progressive, new society. "Let the old one stiffen, we must work hard and create a new one." I wanted to comfort my brother like this, but I didn't say it. I don't pity the decline of a society, I pity those who are old in this society and are nostalgic for the old society; even more pity those who are harmed by the old society without realizing it; they also have a tomorrow in their minds, but this tomorrow has really passed, and they don't know it.

Hometown has changed, and home has also changed! My father tearfully narrated the death of my mother, he said: "Mother hopes you will revitalize the family business······". I want to cry.

Spring Snow

— San Duo

Last year was extremely hot and dry, and it was predicted that this year would be extremely cold. However, the opposite was true, and the climate was warm as spring. The wheat in the countryside has already sprouted, the beans have bloomed, and some peach blossoms are in full bloom. After the great drought, the farmers in various places only place their hopes on this year, and their hopes for snow are as eager as their hopes for clouds and rain in a great drought. The winter is the dormant period for insects. When they have no ability to resist, the snowfall can wipe out the insects that harm rice in one fell swoop. After the beginning of spring, the insects begin to squirm. However, there were two snowflakes after the beginning of spring, which is a great loss in agricultural affairs.

In terms of human affairs, the winter was warm, and the climate was dry. Diphtheria and smallpox were very harmful everywhere. These years, it is pitiful enough to be Chinese people. Natural disasters and man-made disasters have come one after another. Nowadays, the victims in various places are displaced, and this year will be another year of famine. It is really chilling!

However, for the people who live in three-story western-style buildings, snowflakes are irrelevant. Occasionally, they are happy to hold beautiful women and look into the distance, admiring the jade building and the jade palace, or making a grand move to step on the snow to find plum blossoms, which is also equally great!

Frosty and Snowy Morning

— Luo Shan

Near that distant desert, in the foothills of the sunless Western Mountains in the north, when the clear days of the snowy Western Mountains emit a silvery glow, when the light red dawn shines on the snowy Western Mountains, the silvery Western Mountains glow with dazzling golden rosy clouds.

At the foot of the mountains, in the deep valleys where the poplars sway, the shadows of the short trees are shaken, reflected on the snowy hillside, shining with reflected miracles.

Every morning, every morning, in the frost and dew, in the snowy morning, the black shadows are more conspicuously on the hillside.

Under the tiger- and lion-like roaring northwest wind, under the sharp, unyielding cold air, the cold-resistant pine trees, bamboo branches, and yellow-flowered wintersweet are there, looking around and standing on their own.

On the top of the mountain, the white sanatorium for tuberculosis patients with pointed tops stands alone, covered with frost and snow, as if it were a temple of ancient Greece and Rome. The sound of evening prayer bells comes from the ancient temple, shattering the hearts of every traveler with desolation.

The winter wind, whistling a sad tune, lingers under the yellow-flowered wintersweet, beside the holly trees, and on top of the bamboo branches.

There is a hermit who suffers from loneliness. He calls himself Lin Hejing, the "wife of plum blossoms and son of cranes," or Michelangelo, a famous medieval Italian painter and sculptor, and he stumbles on the hillside on frosty and snowy mornings.

In the mountain depressions where snowflakes float like waves and emit silver light, there is a howling sound that is as suppressed as the crying of ghosts and gods.

On his deep face, there is endless sorrow hidden in his heart, and there is no medicine in the world to welcome him.

Near that distant desert, in that sunless Western Mountain, in that clear snowy day, under the reflection of a picture-like flicker, there, there stumbles a spirit of the world.

Gleaning and Others

— Cheng Quan

It is said that it is spring again.

Going to the warm suburbs, perhaps those who grow up in the fields want to find some incomplete smiles and bright images of their youth from the spring grass?

Then, walk quietly on the muddy road; pay attention to a wild flower, a cluster of small grass, and a wandering bird skimming over the water.

Whether memory is the most painful or the sweetest, no one knows: however, I believe that memory is boring. Isn't it? People have no reason when they are bored. Maybe they sit there and break matches one by one, or maybe they walk in the wild and pluck a couple of weeds at will.

Is there ugliness in leisure? Yes, this is undeniable; but we must also understand: in a sick society, "health" does not exist.

(Someone started singing the Wandervogel song, thinking: I wish I could hear the tortuous sound of a six-string guitar? I wish······)

The idea seems to be shaking a little: This spring field of gleaning, what will we get from this?

But this is just like a calm mystery, and the obscure future destiny, which does not allow people to predict at all.

(Natural phenomena are not completely lovely; why do you only look at the pale blue flowers and the tender yellow on the wings of pink butterflies? Is it so easy to forget the mud on the small road on rainy days, and the lightning and thunder in the desolate suburbs at night?

A turbulent wave, a gust of wind, will not be missing on the treacherous journey: they may be as hazy as a sprig of blue flower in the spring field.

Have those who go to the spring suburbs to glean forgotten to worry about the gains of gleaning?)

I am worried, I am afraid.

Perhaps some people have compared "living" to "adventure"? But for me, I always feel that it is more appropriate to compare it to "gleaning in the suburbs". If life is really like an adventure, then we should be much happier; we should always be able to imagine the heroic posture of the explorer, right? Full preparation, rich luggage, energetic interest, and the facts show him··· Ahead is treacherous, we should prepare well.

But will anyone give you such valuable foreshadowing for those who wander on the narrow road of life?

Isn't living like that? Wandering like a leisurely spring suburban gleaner, perhaps everyone wants to have a bright and smooth stroll, picking up some fallen ripe fruits, picking a few green weeds, admiring and savoring them, and their thoughts are carried on a light cloud in the blue sky, slowly drifting away······

But the realization of that dream is not there.

Walking on the muddy path, if you lose your footing, you will fall into the ground; lightning and thunder will strike not far away, and the road is muddy: if you plan to glean something, then it will be withered branches and stumbling pebbles.

And those cold winds and rains that come upon people's inadvertentness?

Walking step by step on the sticky mud road, bravely pick up the unhappy dry branches and stones: people should have an old age: that's right, but when they are old, besides boasting fully about some past plights, what else is there? To say: that is "life experience".

I am worried: Will there also be a warm climate in spring? Does anyone dare to guarantee that the harvest of the spring field gleaner is gratifying?

(What is terrible is: the dryness, wetness, coldness and warmth of the seasons and)

The wind, rain, darkness and brightness of the climate.

In this era, even spring is unreliable. I remembered a poem:

"Few sunny days in spring, many fallen flowers in March!"

The gleaners in the spring wilderness must worry.

Old Ju's Words

— Bo Xiang

"What did the past year give you?" If someone asked Old Ju this way, then he could frankly answer you: "A pair of white shoes, a gray cloth robe."

"What else?"

"Tens of millions of pairs of more contemptuous eyes."

"What else?"

"Extreme insomnia and severe neurasthenia."

This is all he has harvested throughout the year.

Although he was not present in the first minute that he was given white shoes, in the long nights of insomnia, he could look at the top of the account and connect the fragmented pieces told to him by his family to create a fantasy······

How tragic that scene was! A person who had not yet reached the age of choking choked so quickly.

That was not right. From whatever point of view, with his old man's kindness and loyalty, he should not have summed up his life so quickly; if God knew, then it should admit: This is an accidental mistake.

But because of this accidental mistake, Old Ju's fate was decided. There was no smile on his face. Even in front of the few people who gave him bread to eat, he had to reluctantly practice a set: the smile that was forced to be pieced together with the flesh on his face was painful, like the smile of a woman selling herself on the night street. What it preserves inside is: tears, is sorrow. If you have ever met him, then you can guess his fate from his clothes: he is wearing white shoes that have been dyed gray by dust and a cloth robe stained with stains. The beard under his chin is darker than his age by a factor of two, and even though it is the New Year, he is not happy to fix it.

Really, the unfortunate iron hat is tightly tied to him, and even others feel unfortunate when they see it. This is not an exaggeration. Many month friends are like this, especially near the end of the year. They are all afraid that Old Ju will ask them to borrow money. They know that Old Ju's family situation is not good. When they hear him talk about that unfortunate story, this is what he often talks about, they will look at him with pity, no, actually with contempt and walk away. They all underestimated Old Ju. He just couldn't close his psychological depression and told others about his experience. He is not the kind of person who asks to borrow. He is born with a stubborn temper, willing to tighten his belt, unwilling to bow his body and ask people to open his mouth. He clearly controls the few money he earns with his labor. What does it matter if he is poor?

But others did not understand him, and his personality was dimmed by poverty.

(Accepting people's contempt aggrievedly? Some are unwilling. What to do? Unless you poke out your own eyes!)

He thought so alone, waking up in the quiet night. People were originally contemptuous of him, but now it has doubled. Of course, he knows the reason for this doubling: it is related to white shoes. So the scene of the old man choking is repeatedly shown in his meninges. Every night, he can always hear the first hour of the morning.

The more he is despised by people, the more he thinks like this, the more he thinks like this, the more he suffers from insomnia, and the more he suffers from neurasthenia: many gray cells circulate and surge in his carotid arteries, and he has spent the past year so grayly.

From this year on, he is prepared to keep his mouth shut and not talk to others about his own experiences.

Classical Chinese

Feng Mingquan National Studies

Zhongxi (1040) 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM

Han Yu's Memorial on the Bone of the Buddha (Continued)

However, the common people are foolish and ignorant, easily confused and difficult to understand. If they see Your Majesty like this, they will think that you sincerely serve the Buddha. Everyone will say that the Emperor is a great sage and still reverently believes. Who are the common people? How can they not cherish their lives, burn the top of their heads, burn their fingers, hundreds and thousands in groups, undress and scatter money from morning till night, imitating each other, fearing to be late, old and young running around, abandoning their occupations. If you do not immediately prohibit it, and go through other things, there will be those who cut off their arms and hurt their bodies as offerings, damaging customs and spreading laughter in all directions, which is not a trivial matter. The Buddha was originally a barbarian, whose language was not understood in China, whose clothes were different, whose mouth did not speak the words of the former kings, whose body did not wear the clothes of the former kings, who did not know the nurturing of rulers and ministers, the affection of fathers and sons. If he were still alive today, obeying his country's orders, and came to the capital to pay tribute, Your Majesty would tolerate and receive him, but after one audience, one banquet, one gift of clothes, he would be escorted out of the border, not allowing him to confuse the public.

9:00 AM to 9:30 AM (Tang Poetry) Feeling Encounter Four (Five Ancient Poems Volume One)

In Jiangnan there are tangerines, Still green forests through the winter, Is it the warm climate, Or does it have a heart for the cold season? Can be recommended to honored guests, But how to overcome the deep obstacles? Fate is only what is encountered, The cycle cannot be found, In vain to say plant peaches and plums, How can this tree have no shade?

1:00 PM to 2:00 PM (Mencius Exhausting the Heart) Yangzi Takes for Me Chapter

Sun Deyu University

Navigation (1180) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Knowing where to stop, then there is stability; after stability, then there can be tranquility; after tranquility, then there can be peace; after peace, then there can be deliberation; after deliberation, then there can be gain.

Stopping is the place where one should stop, that is, where ultimate goodness lies. Knowing it, then the will has direction. Tranquility means the mind does not move rashly. Peace means being at peace wherever one is. Deliberation means being detailed and thorough in handling affairs. Gain means obtaining what one should stop at.

Things have roots and branches, affairs have beginnings and ends, knowing what comes first and what comes later is close to the way.

Illustrious virtue is the root, renewing the people is the branch, knowing where to stop is the beginning, being able to gain is the end, the root and the beginning come first, the branches and the end come later, this concludes the meaning of the above sections.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Necessary Knowledge (Continued)

— Xi Liu

Some extras think that they are just [air], so they don't need to memorize lines. Their ideal of [air] is good. In the silent film era, air originally did not speak, but since the invention of sound films, audiences hope that even those who act as air or background should have a voice. Therefore, air in the sound film era must also speak, laugh, and sing.

For example, if you are shooting a film about high society, then everything on the set must represent the splendor of Fifth Avenue, and extras cannot be an exception. Because the director may turn the camera around at any time, panning here and there, and the microphone may be placed here or there at any time, the extras don't know, so even when they are not in the camera's angle, their speech should be careful and conform to the standards of high society. It's not like the silent film era anymore. In the silent film era, an actor could say: [Hey, where's the beer?] and the subtitle would become: [Baby, I love you]. Because at that time, all that mattered was that the mouth could move.

Also, when filming, your demeanor must match the clothes you are wearing and the words you are speaking. An actor must know the customs of different people, such as how Easterners smoke cigarettes with the tip pointing upwards, while Westerners smoke with the tip pointing downwards, and so on.

Some films also have foreign scenes. The extras used in those scenes are French, Italian, Spanish, etc. They not only have to look authentic, but also be able to speak a few foreign languages, understand the customs of each country, and the games and songs of each country, etc. A versatile extra can play many kinds of roles. Even if we only talk about American-style roles, there are countless types. A woman may play a debutante today, a dancer tomorrow, and something else the day after tomorrow. But she must be careful not to confuse their personalities.

Memorizing lines is certainly something extras need to practice, but that's not enough. In the sound film era, almost every film has some music, so it would be very helpful for extras to be able to sing a few songs and play a few instruments for their future. Dancing, no matter what kind, is also very useful, because you don't necessarily need to dance in a film, but a person who can dance will have a very lively and natural figure and gait. Body language also occupies a very important position in film. Any director will agree that body language represents a person's personality and has the same potential for expression as a person's voice.

A good extra should be familiar with all kinds of games and sports, both indoor and outdoor, although they don't necessarily need to have deep knowledge. Film sets need people to play cards, tennis, golf, ride horses, and swim every day. Even if they are not useful for the time being, these sports can keep your body active and your mind sharp.

In addition, a person must have a reasonable income when working as an extra, because extras don't necessarily have work every day, and the income is very limited. At the same time, in addition to daily expenses, you must also buy clothes, hire teachers, etc. Working as an extra can't be considered a profession, but it's like going to a vocational school to be a prospective star. Of course, you can't expect the school to support you. Ten or eight years ago, working as an extra could be considered a profession and you could live off of it. But there were fewer extras back then, and the film scenes were long and needed a lot of people, so it was easy to become an actor. But now everything is different.

You may think that it was easier to become an actor back then, so the extras from that time have all become stars now. But that's not the case. If they don't know how to learn, they probably wouldn't even be able to keep their positions as extras now. So, learning is essential. When sound films were first invented, all films were musicals, and actors had to set aside time to learn to speak, sing, and dance in addition to their usual day and night performances. I remember that Alice White used to film during the day and practice dancing, singing, and playing the piano at home at night, and had to memorize the lines for the next day, often to the point of exhaustion. Alice White was like this, and all the big stars had to go through this stage. Otherwise, they would be naturally eliminated.

But what is the reward for this hard work? Victory, fame! As long as the film industry exists, there will be millions of young men and women fighting and sacrificing for that unique reward. How can you blame those twenty-odd young men and women for staying in Hollywood and not leaving? (End)

Film Reviews

Review of [Nurses' Story]

— You Jing

TheWhiteParade丨Cathay Release

From the perspective of dramatic theme, director's skill, and actor's technique, this [Nurses' Story] is a watchable film. In the regressive call for [women to return to the home], and in the face of the general naivety of young girls wavering between [being a pampered wife and daughter-in-law] or [dedicating themselves to sacred social service], we must emphasize its significance as a recommendation.

Here, the playwrights Souya Levie and Ernel Pagch, in depicting the student life of a nursing training school, show that the meaning of a woman's existence does not lie in the affections of men, but in the great and sacred cause of serving the masses.

The story begins with a group of lively, even naughty, girls entering a nursing school. In a life of strict management and heavy workload, they feel tired and bored; at the same time, the progress of knowledge, the vision of their careers, and the life of the group give them infinite interest and comfort.

Here, the producers depicted the various personalities, mutual influences, group activities, and private lives of this group of girls, as well as the humor of the serious faces of the teachers and the playful hearts of the girls intersecting, with great delicacy, care, and depth. They are both realistic and faithful records, and fresh and insightful excavations.

As the plot unfolds, it shifts from a collective narrative to individual development. It begins with the melancholy Xuewei, who commits suicide in a tragic act. And Qiongying, who is lively, kind, and enthusiastic, is tricked by another classmate for falsely claiming that the wealthy young man Raona, who was reported in the newspaper, is her lover, which leads to a real romance. Finally, in a man's passionate kiss, the laughter of many babies, and the sorrowful faces of patients, she moves from contradiction and distress to an honest and resolute commitment to social service, to complete the highest task of humanity.

The above story is extremely simple, but the producers use indirect and vivid descriptions to make the film extremely lively, bright, and full.

Director Irving Cumming initially used the solemn and quiet school gate to show the atmosphere inside and outside the school. The Puritanical, thin female superintendent, and the broad-minded, both strict and kind female manager; the candlelight in the solemn ceremony, the silence in the practice room, the laughter in front of the cafe; the carefulness towards patients, the teasing and playfulness towards companions... In terms of emotions, atmosphere, and personality, the director has put in considerable effort and achieved good results. Especially in terms of contrast and highlighting.

But it is not without flaws. Although the screenwriter avoided the clichéd ending of [lovers finally getting married], the fact that Qiongying said someone was her lover and that they actually fell in love at first sight still did not escape the Hollywood-style love performance. After Qiongying graduated, when she refused Raona's marriage proposal, Raona had already left in disappointment, and the playwright had to have a doctor come to comfort her, which was too obviously preachy. In terms of directing, the repeated appearances of the manager seriously reciting the school rules added to the solemn atmosphere of the play and earned the audience's laughter, but this was not without loss. The emphasis on church etiquette in the school ceremony, and its repeated performance, is really [adding legs to a snake] in terms of dramatic effect.

Due to the appropriate (casting), the actors each achieved good results. The female lead Loretta Young's passionate and compassionate girl image is more pleasing than her performance in [The Prodigal]. Perhaps it is because this [Nurse's Story] is a woman's play? The male lead John Bowers is only average. On the other hand, the school authorities, one thin and one fat, have achieved just the right effect.

Review of [Hell's Highway]

— Ji Han

HEllSHighway丨Shanghai

Mervyn LeRoy's [I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang] shocked the American film industry, and under this influence, RKO's [Hell's Highway] appeared. Although we can glimpse commercial competition here, its starting point is to expose the darkness of American prisons, and audiences with a sense of justice do not dislike the repeated use of the same subject matter.

At the beginning of the play, we read the following subtitles: "Made to expose the darkness of the modern Middle Ages." This explanation of the topic clearly shows the author's intention to expose the abuse of prisoners under American law, and to further represent the suffering prisoners in demanding improved treatment from the government. We repeatedly see the warden and the road construction engineer inflicting cruel punishments on the prisoners: flogging with whips, locking them in sweatboxes until they suffocate to death, and when they are too exhausted to work, the guards think they are lazy. For losing a spoon, they are not given food. Extremely heavy shackles never leave their bodies. On the other hand, we also see the warden leisurely playing the violin, and the engineer writing a letter to the machine factory thanking them for the exquisite sweatbox. Under such cruel treatment, we see the prisoners harboring extreme resentment in their hearts. They shout loudly, "No food, no work!" They demand spoons in the dining hall, and when a spoon is lost, the warden orders that no spoons be issued. They can no longer endure this cruel treatment, they resist, they are willing to risk their lives to seize freedom. We see that the spoon becomes a sharp blade to kill the warden, they seize the guards' guns, they have a planned and organized prison break. In a shout filled with red light, their group of lawless people riot. Naturally, their resistance ultimately fails, and they are killed and wounded under the massive encirclement of the police. Although we see the sadness of their failure, the prospect of victory unfolds in this spray of blood.

Of course, this is not without its shortcomings. Due to the director's lack of magnificent power, and also due to the script's lack of rigorous structure, we feel that the performance is not tense enough, not stimulating enough, at least after seeing [I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang], we always feel that it lacks flavor. More importantly, there are still some inaccuracies in the content. The protagonist Duke is a hero in the film. Although the playwright explains that he has been imprisoned several times, he does not write him as an unpardonable person. On the contrary, under the cruel treatment, he is confident that there is a need to break out of prison, but for the sake of his brother's happiness, he is contradictory and temporarily suspends his heroic actions. Related to this is the fact that the government official finally arrests the engineer, implying that the government is determined to improve the treatment of prisoners, but it is only the wardens and guards who are acting arbitrarily. Improving the living conditions of prisoners was originally a requirement of the play, but unfortunately this hope will inevitably turn into a bubble in the eyes of the artist before the old system is destroyed.

What makes us feel gratified in the end is that the playwright did not distort the conclusion to an unacceptable degree. Although the hero Duke voluntarily returns to prison carrying his brother on his back, he does not casually receive an amnesty. In the iron gate, it is implied that the hero has fallen, assuming that he is completely submissive. On the other hand, the slaves have risen up, and the prisoners ridicule Duke for betraying the interests of his fellows. In the bloody tragedy, it is explained that today's slaves cannot live in inhuman treatment.

Although we cannot be entirely satisfied with this film, it is ultimately worthy of people's attention, and it has achieved great success in terms of exposure.

Film Novel

David Copperfield (6)

— Willow Village

Although David wanted to comfort himself by thinking that what he imagined might not be true, he clearly saw that every time Amy saw Steerforth, a strange light appeared in her eyes. She didn't have that light when she saw Ham, even though Ham was her future husband. So, later, when Ham received the bad news, David seemed to have foreseen it. When Ham handed David a letter and asked him to read it to everyone, his throat was hoarse. He didn't dare to look up at the old fisherman, Ham, Mr. Peggotty, and the others. He read the letter word by word. It said:

"You love me more than I deserve. By the time you read this letter, I will have left you. I will never return unless I have become a noble lady and return with him. I have failed your great kindness. Please find someone else who can return your sincere love, and love her. Please just think of me as having died young and buried in an unknown place. And please tell Uncle that I have never loved him as dearly as I do now."

David finished reading, and the paper fluttered from his hands. Ham stood up, as if he wanted to say something, but at this moment, everyone was looking at the old fisherman. He looked furious and terrifying, and asked in a trembling voice, "Who is he? I want to know his name! Who is he?" David remembered the many things he and his classmates had said before, so he said, "Steerforth." The old fisherman heard this, immediately turned around, and walked towards the door. As he walked, he said, "I'm going to find my Amy, no matter how far away. I will find her and bring her back. No one can stop me." Of course, no one could stop him. So he set off to start searching, traveled all over the world, and endured countless years of wind and frost.

After the old fisherman left, David couldn't think of anything else to do but quietly leave that place where they had once gathered and celebrated, and return to London. In London, month after month passed. Although he was often worried about his friends at Doctor's Commons, his own life was filled with important things. His usual writing aspirations had now received some reward, because one of his novels had been published in a monthly magazine. But this victory was nothing, because Dora had agreed to be his wife. So he immediately ran to Canterbury to tell his aunt, Betsey, and his teacher, Wickfield, and Agnes, about the happiness Dora had given him. He was so intoxicated with his own happiness that he didn't even notice the sorrow and disappointment in Agnes's eyes.

Poor Agnes, since David left, she had become uninterested in everything. Her father had brought Uriah Heep in as a partner in his business. Uriah seemed to manipulate Wickfield at will. Uriah slept in the room David used to sleep in. Although Wickfield himself said that his promotion of Uriah was his own wish, no one believed that. However, Micawber couldn't tell David what power Uriah had to play Wickfield in the palm of his hand, to the point where he was so bold and reckless as to ask Wickfield to marry Agnes to him. This was Wickfield's first outburst of anger in many years. This ignorant Heep actually wanted to be matched with Agnes. Even Uriah, the humble Uriah, knew afterwards that he had gone too far.

The day of David and Dora's wedding arrived. At that time, even Wickfield's family and the difficulties in Wickfield's home were temporarily put out of David's mind. Dora, his baby wife, was a woman with only looks and no ability to do anything. She couldn't even keep track of the daily household accounts. She didn't know how to cook, let alone manage household affairs or servants. Soon, his home was in complete disarray. David's study was a mess, but David was deeply in love with Dora and their affection was unwavering. (To be continued)

The Shanghai News Extra Edition Construction Weekly

A General Overview of Shanghai Construction in the Past Year (1)

— Yang Dehui

Time flies like an arrow, and another year has passed so quickly. Looking back at Shanghai's construction in the past year, although the world's economic panic is still deeply serious, and the domestic rural bankruptcy has been compounded by an unprecedented drought, making it even more acute, Shanghai's construction is still very developed. This may make people suspicious, but in Shanghai, the base of imperialism, the development of construction is a natural phenomenon, and there is nothing to doubt. Precisely because of this, it can further promote the progress and development of Shanghai's construction. Actions speak louder than words. The facts are before our eyes. The completion of tall buildings and the completion of new halls and houses appear one after another. We can also observe from the population that it is increasing every day. According to the population statistics for November of last year, the total number of people was 3,446,4528, an increase of 15,374 people compared to the 3,449,154 people in October of the same year. Do these not prove the reasons for the development of Shanghai's construction? Therefore, no one will deny the development of Shanghai's construction. Now, the total value of construction in the past eight years is listed below, which can also give us a clear understanding of Shanghai's construction situation.

1927: 15,263,552 taels

1928: 32,356,986 taels

1929: 45,386,682 taels

1930: 71,511,816 taels

1931: 62,351,250 taels

1932: 35,541,009 taels

1933: 72,175,000 yuan

1934: 55,880,000 yuan

In the table above, the total value of construction last year only includes the total from January to the end of October, and November and December have not yet been included! If we calculate the total number of months for ten months, then, of course, there will be another 11 million yuan to be added for November and December. Although it is slightly lower than the value in 1933, we should understand here that the decline in the price of building materials last year compared to 1933 is an ironclad fact. Not only building materials, but also the prices of everything, were also slightly lower than in 1933! Therefore, Shanghai's construction last year was still developing. Now, according to the current administrative divisions, Shanghai's construction can be divided into the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the city area. In order to understand the construction situation in each district last year, we have to discuss it separately below. In fact, this is worth studying.

Now, let's first talk about the Public Concession! The total construction amount in the Public Concession in the ten months of last year was 25,212,000 yuan, accounting for 50% of the total construction amount in the city. Originally, Shanghai's construction could be represented by the Public Concession alone. Therefore, its construction costs have always been more than half of the total over the years. This is due to the environment. In the first six months of last year, new construction projects were worth 16,233,000 yuan, accounting for 45% of the total value of the city. Among these, the central district accounted for 31%, the western Shanghai district accounted for 34%, the eastern Shanghai district accounted for 30%, and the northern Shanghai district accounted for only 5%. Compared with the same period in 1933, it decreased by 10%. In the construction cost of 16,233,000 yuan, a total of 2,013 construction licenses were issued, including 88 Chinese-style houses built in the central district, 44 Western-style shops, 1 Western-style residence, 2 bank buildings, 1 office, 1 factory, and 3 garages. In the eastern Shanghai district, 460 Chinese-style halls and houses, 1 Western-style residence, 4 staff dormitories, 12 factories, 1 yarn factory, 46 other factory buildings, 6 warehouses, and 1 office were built. In the western Shanghai district, 935 Chinese-style houses, 93 Western-style shops, 97 Western-style residences, 2 apartments, 4 staff dormitories, 3 factories, 3 other factory buildings, 1 school, 3 warehouses, and 27 garages were built. In the northern Shanghai district, 164 Chinese-style halls and houses, 7 Western-style shops, 1 apartment, 1 school, and 1 garage were built. As for the halls and houses demolished and rebuilt, there were 713 Chinese-style halls and houses and 45 Western-style halls and houses. The construction value in July and August was 5,075,000 yuan, with 2,079,000 yuan in July and 2,996,000 yuan in August, which was better than July. The construction in the western Shanghai district accounted for more than 50% of the total value in the two months, including 153 Chinese-style halls and houses, 26 Western-style residences, 1 hotel, 3 schools, and 3 factories. In the eastern Shanghai district, 326 Chinese-style residences, 41 Western-style shops, 3 factories, 23 other factory halls and houses, and 4 warehouses were built. As for the construction value in the central district, it was 648,000 yuan, and in the northern Shanghai district, it was 325,000 yuan. Although no construction classification is given to us clearly, we can also know the general situation of its construction. The construction in September and October was slightly lower than in the same period in 1933, only 3,905,000 yuan, and the eastern Shanghai district accounted for the majority! A total of 206 Chinese-style halls and houses, 5 offices, 12 Western-style residences, and 18 industrial factory halls were built. In the western Shanghai district, more than 30 Western-style halls and houses were built. The central district accounted for 23% of the construction amount, and the northern Shanghai district accounted for only 7%. Here, the details of the construction in the Public Concession are clear. And the result is that the construction in the western Shanghai district and the eastern Shanghai district is more developed than in the central district. This is because the buildings in the central district are already everywhere, and we all know that there is no room for construction. Therefore, we have to build in the eastern district and the western district. The eastern district and the western district have become the factory area and residential area of Shanghai, so the construction of their buildings is mostly factory halls and houses and residences. As mentioned above, the buildings in the eastern Shanghai district and the western Shanghai district in the ten months of last year can clearly show the trend of their buildings. Now, the out-of-bounds road construction area negotiated by the authorities is the eastern Shanghai district and the western Shanghai district of the Public Concession, because the eastern Shanghai district and the western Shanghai district have more room for development than the central district, so most of the construction last year was also in these two districts.

Steel and Its Protection Methods (Part 1)

— Qin

Steel has long been used in construction, but its importance and ease of use have become more and more prominent in recent decades. Roughly speaking, its advantages are five: 1) non-combustible, 2) no shrinkage, 3) strong material, 4) no need to worry about worm infestation, 5) easy to make various styles. There are many common steel frame structures, and more than a hundred types have been invented and successfully used by architects over the years, but they all do not go beyond the four categories of rolled steel profiles, steel plates, steel sheets, or steel bars. Their application may be for roofs, or as wall frames, or as materials for window frames, or for the laying of floors, etc. There is also the invention of stainless steel in recent times, which is widely used in kitchens, bathrooms, and other places, and its development seems to be still in full swing.

Steel is so important in construction and so widely used, so if we want to explore its physics and understand its use in detail, it cannot be fully covered in a few words. What is described here is only thin steel material, including only steel sheets and steel bars. However. This kind of steel material is indeed the focus of modern architects' research on its application methods to improve construction, so it is no coincidence that we choose to discuss this.

Steel sheets and steel bars have many similarities, the only difference is their length, width, and narrowness. Ordinary people often have a doubt, what is the difference between steel plates and steel sheets? Regarding this point, if we only use their thickness as a boundary, it is indeed confusing. According to American regulations, the thickness of steel sheets should not exceed the thickness of standard No. 10 copper wire, which is roughly less than 9/64 inches, while the thinnest limit of steel plates is 3/16 inches. However, this regulation has determined the difference between steel sheets and steel plates, and there are even clearer distinctions, that is, depending on the required properties of the material. Steel plates are mostly used for their strength and toughness, while steel sheets require more surface perfection, and there are large differences in manufacturing methods.

Steel sheets and steel bars must have the following three elements:

1) Strength for construction

2) Connectability and methods

3) Durability (To be continued)

Medieval Architecture (Part 2)

— Qin

The Gothic architectural method is also ingeniously varied, unlike the Romanesque style which is so rigid. Its variation often depends on the location, scale, and other special circumstances. When we see the Acropolis temple built by the Greeks in Athens, its roof had to be low and flat because it was meant to suit its position. However, Gothic temples, built on the peaks of mountains in sacred areas, not only stand on the mountain, with a magnificent atmosphere, but also add beauty to the mountains and rivers, enhancing the beauty of nature. This means that people's psychology is gradually loving a kind of adventurous, mysterious, and strange architectural form. These characteristics all require people to express them with courageous strength, so we should not be surprised that the origin and development of this Gothic architectural style is in the north of Europe, where the climate is cold, and the people are strong and full of adventurous spirit.

The rise of the Gothic style was very rapid, and its spread throughout Europe was also very extensive, creating an indelible page in the history of architecture. However, the times are constantly progressing, human thought is constantly changing, and the world's culture is constantly advancing and expanding. Therefore, this Gothic architecture, after three hundred years, eventually became an inevitable laggard. Their previous prosperity no longer exists. Its courageous and adventurous characteristics have also been abandoned, and at the same time, people have another kind of concept and ambition growing in their endless historical journey.

New-Style Residential Architecture and Sanitary Design (Continued)

— Xi Hao

The relationship of lighting is even more important to the health of the whole body and mind. Every engineer should carefully study the volume of the residence and the configuration of the lighting. Excessively strong light will cause your nerves to be over-stimulated. Strong light will cause your nerves to be over-stimulated and produce an abnormal mental response. Too dim light will cause your spirit to be unexpectedly consumed. Both of these situations are harmful to health. The configuration of the wall's reflective effect is even more important in lighting. All excessively exciting decorations must be avoided as much as possible. Pale yellow or egg-yellow decorations have been proven to have excellent reflective effects.

The third major issue in sanitary design is the equipment of the entire residence. A convenient supply of water and electricity is sufficient to save the owner's energy and increase a lot of comfort. The bathroom is an indispensable thing in new-style residential architecture. It is often seen that a very good residence has good equipment, but lacks the most needed bathroom, and loses its value. The equipment in the bathroom does not have to be very luxurious, "easy to clean" is the most important issue in bathroom design.

Secondly, a suitably sized courtyard is a necessary accessory in new-style architecture. The owner can use it as a place for physical and mental recreation, or as a small-scale exercise yard. In new-style residences in Europe and the United States, small lawns or dirt courtyards are equipped, where family members and children can play tennis, small football, and other games, which not only increases the joy of life, but also gradually exercises the physique of the entire family. Our country's engineers may as well adopt this excellent sanitary design as much as possible.

The above are just the largest points, and are what general architects should strictly pay attention to.

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor: Recently, since the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has strictly enforced the Industrial Technician Registration Law, it is almost difficult to become a technician without a formal school diploma. Especially for architectural engineering talents, there is a greater lack. Therefore, universities in the country have added architecture departments to meet the needs. In the past year, several new architectural specialty evening schools have appeared, even in Shanghai alone. Among them, such as the Shanghai University Architecture Specialty Evening School on Yuanmingyuan Road, and the Architectural Engineering Evening School of the Lester Institute in Hongkou, both have comprehensive equipment and complete courses, and invite domestic architectural experts to help young people who have no opportunity to study in order to seek a bright future. However, there are also quite a few people who use this as a speculative business, use false words to attract students, use foreigners to swagger and deceive, collect large amounts of tuition fees, and mislead young people. Recently, such as a certain vocational school found on Jiangxi Road, which widely distributes leaflets, saying that it teaches higher architectural subjects, with only four hours of instruction per week, and graduates in half a year, and shamelessly uses registration as a technician with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce as bait, charging as much as dozens of yuan per month, its fraudulent behavior is self-evident. I hope that our architectural youth will not be deceived by it, and that the education authorities should also find ways to ban it. If you are kind enough to publish the above situation, I will be publicly grateful. I wish you peace. I humbly request above.
